(September 11th) The livelihood of overseas Chinese in Nanyang is becoming increasingly narrow.

British Authorities Will Extend the Restriction Period, Dutch Authorities Will Amend the Import Regulations 52

Shantou correspondence: The unemployment problem has recently become a serious issue for various countries around the world. Waves are rising, and the overseas Chinese in Nanyang English and Dutch colonies are the first to be affected by this. According to statistics from the Singapore government, in the past ten years, a total of 2,301,869 overseas Chinese have gone to Singapore from Shantou, Hong Kong, Xiamen, and Haikou. The number of overseas Chinese returning home is 700,209. The number of overseas Chinese increased by 2,316,660 in Singapore in ten years. Therefore, the Singapore government restricted the entry of Chinese workers from September 1st due to the decline in the prices of rubber and tin blocks, stating that it would be a three-month trial period. If the market can be stabilized, it will continue to be extended. This matter is of great importance to the future of our country's overseas Chinese. It has not been heard whether our diplomatic authorities have had any communication with the British government on the matter. A reporter from a Shantou newspaper interviewed the British consulate yesterday. According to the British consulate, this regulation will be extended indefinitely.

In Thailand, strict new restrictions have been implemented since this month. The French colonies in Annam have even stricter regulations restricting overseas Chinese. Yesterday, the Nanxing Wheel arrived in Shantou and 134 overseas Chinese were deported. More than 90 of them were from Guangzhou. The Guangzhou-Zhao Association provided accommodation for them and issued 3 yuan per person to send them back to their hometowns. The rest were accommodated by the Shantou Overseas Chinese Hospital and various charitable halls. According to the overseas Chinese who were deported back to Shantou, the Annam government forced local overseas Chinese to pay a personal tax of 33.5 yuan per year. They must pay tax once a month. If the payment is delayed by one day, there will be a fine of 2 yuan. If they do not pay for one month, they will be arrested and imprisoned to work as street cleaners and road builders. As far as they know, no less than three to four hundred overseas Chinese have been arrested and imprisoned.

In addition, due to Singapore's restrictions on Chinese workers, the Dutch colonies of Batavia and other commercial ports in Nanyang have also increased their strict measures against China. According to those who returned to Shantou from Batavia, new arrivals must understand the following new rules: (1) the exit passport must be signed by the Dutch consul in China; (2) each person must pay 100 Dutch Indian guilders, which has been increased to 150 guilders this year; (3) when landing, there must be a store or employer to guarantee; (4) high-ranking merchants with capital industries do not need a guarantee; (5) they must not carry books and documents with political meaning; (6) all store employees, workers, and teachers must be guaranteed by a local store to enter the country; (7) old customers entering the country who return after the deadline will be treated as new customers and perform the above procedures; (8) pay an additional 50 guilders landing fee; (9) the original residence permit must be signed by the Civil Affairs Office and the主管官廳 otherwise it will be invalid; (10) old customers returning to Shantou must also obtain a passport when leaving the country and have it signed by the Dutch consulate, and verify the return passport issued by the Chinese consulate in the Netherlands. Absolutely do not bring books related to politics, otherwise they will be deported. The above are the new rules of the Dutch government for overseas Chinese. If our government does not negotiate to cancel them, I am afraid that the livelihood of overseas Chinese in Nanyang will become increasingly narrow and even cut off. (September 11th)

Fujian Army Attacks Dehua 53

Xiamen correspondence: Since Fang Shengtao went to Yongchun, the military situation in southern Fujian has been that the front launched a general offensive against Dehua on the 1st. The main force was Chen Guohui's unit of six battalions, about 1,500 people. The northern route was one division, Lin Qinglong's supplementary regiment, about 800 people. The western route was the first regiment of one division, Wang Zuqing's unit, about 1,500 people, combined with artillery and machine guns, about 4,000 people. Xu Feilong was entrenched in the earthen fort. The provincial army attacked the earthen fort with artillery. On the morning of the 5th, the first division, under the cover of artillery, charged to Zhangqian, three miles away from the city. On the 6th, they continued to shell it, with six mortars, two deployed on the 牛頭寨, one on the 西門宫顶, two on the 洞寨, one on the 北門頭. Five large guns were seven-borns, one deployed on the 牛頭寨, one deployed on the 洞寨, one remotely attacking the city. A total of 108 mortar shells and 86 large gun shells were fired. In addition, six water machine guns, three dry machine guns, and infantry launched assaults on the five key points of 牛頭寨, 西門宫顶, 砲壘洞寨, 北門頭 and earthen city. The Xiamen Naval Aviation Office also sent planes to Yongchun to transfer to Dehua on the 4th, 5th, and 6th to scout the enemy's situation and scatter Fang Shengtao's message to the army and people of Dehua. It briefly stated that Xu Feilong was guilty of rebellion and that the people must move to the countryside to avoid artillery fire. All of Xu's followers who can repent and return will not only not be punished but also heavily rewarded. Those who can capture Xu or offer his head will be rewarded with 5,000 yuan, and those who lead the crowd to return will be paid ten yuan per gun and allowed to be reorganized. The planes also dropped bombs on 雷公寨, destroying one earthen fort. The artillery battles continued on the 7th and 8th. On the 9th, the main force of Chen Guohui's unit occupied Caopuwe, cutting off the traffic between Dehua City and Xu Feilong's old nest, Sanban. On the same day, Lin Qinglong occupied Xidun and Moshi Ridge, cutting off the traffic between the north gate of Dehua City and Jiaoxi. On the 11th, Wang Zuqing's regiment occupied Tangsai outside the west gate. Therefore, Dehua City has been surrounded on all sides. The war in the fort lasted for four days. Lu Xingbang transported 30 dan of bullets from Datian to Xu Feilong, but they were intercepted by Zhang Ying's unit of Huang Qilan's department on Xishan. Therefore, Xu's unit was extremely short of bullets. It is expected that Dehua City will be captured soon. Once Dehua is down, the Liu Heding division will advance to the upper reaches of Datian, and jointly attack Youxi from Yongtai and Minqing. (12th)

Page 10

Jiaoji Railway Holds Section Affairs Meeting 54

Jinan correspondence: Since the war, the Jiaoji Railway has barely been open to traffic, and freight transport has only recovered seven or eight percent. The traffic order is also extremely chaotic. Tan Shukui, the deputy director of the Jiaoji Railway Vehicle Department, came to Jinan a few days ago to decide to hold a section affairs meeting of the Vehicle Department in Jinan. The meeting was held in the Jiaoji Station VIP room at 9:00 am today (13th). The attendees were Tan Shukui, deputy director of the Vehicle Department; Su Bubin, director of the first section; Ma Defang, director of the second section; Li Binting, director of the third section; Liu Dide, director of the fourth section; and Sui Jiwu, chief of the Vehicle Department's Documents Section; Wei Xin, chief of the Business Section; Li Shantang, chief of the Audit Section; Lu Jiaju, chief of the Telecommunications Section; Yuan Chucai, chief of the Traffic Stock; and Mr. Kagayama, the Japanese director of the Vehicle Department, was also present. After Chairman Tan Shukui opened the meeting, the chairman reported that the railway had suffered heavy losses in the war, and it was difficult to maintain the status quo, and the railway's life was tied to the Vehicle Department, so the department should hold a section affairs meeting to discuss traffic order, maintain income, and other matters. In previous years, section affairs meetings were held in Qingdao, but this time, due to the war, it was necessary to understand the situation of each station to provide reference material for the meeting so that good results could be discussed. This was not very relevant to the section chiefs, but it was very important for the colleagues in the department, so it was moved to Jinan. Afterwards, various issues concerning vehicle affairs were raised and discussed separately: (1) Regarding freight transport: due to various reasons, the railway is short of freight cars, and has only recovered seven or eight percent. In order to increase income and facilitate freight transport, the railway should find ways to remedy the situation. It was decided that in addition to requesting the military authorities to return military vehicles, the existing vehicles should be used to increase turnover rate, reduce the parking time at each station, and accelerate loading and unloading to free up time to increase the number of trips and remedy freight transport. (2) Regarding order: in the past, soldiers were not allowed to ride the train without a ticket. It is not surprising that this could not be implemented after the war. However, the railway's income depends entirely on the Vehicle Department, so the traffic order should be restored immediately to maintain income. It was decided that the issue of soldiers riding the train without a ticket had been agreed by Sun Junzhang (Tongxuan) of the 12th Army and Cao Junzhang (Fulin) of the 14th Army, and they were allowed to instruct and strictly prohibit it. The department should now strictly formulate ticket inspection methods and issue orders to implement them conscientiously. (3) Regarding hygiene: the hygiene facilities on the railway's trains are more complete than other railways and can be implemented conscientiously. This should be done to improve the sanitation after the war. It was decided that the section chiefs should be responsible for instructing the staff at each station and on the trains to strictly implement cleanliness and hygiene, and to investigate and prohibit passengers from engaging in unhygienic behavior. The section chiefs must also inspect from time to time and not treat it as a mere formality. (4) Regarding staff: how should the staff in the war zone who served at risk during the war and those who temporarily evaded responsibility be handled? It was decided that the staff in the war zone suffered great losses both mentally and physically and should be transferred to the rear for rest or to a station with simpler affairs for adjustment. The staff who temporarily evaded responsibilities should be punished according to the circumstances. The meeting adjourned at 1:00 pm. I visited Mr. Tan Shukui after the meeting. According to Tan, the decisions made at this section affairs meeting are the most important matters at present, because the railway's business prospects are extremely difficult to be optimistic about. In previous years, the railway's income was about 11 million yuan per year, excluding salary expenses, material expenses, and daily interest of 2.4 million yuan, there was a net profit of about one million yuan. This year's business income is expected to increase by one-third compared to last year, reaching more than 14 million yuan. However, the income has already been reduced by more than 3 million due to the war. Although the income may be barely 11 million by the end of this year, the railway employees have increased their salaries, and during the war period in the war zone, the employees were paid three times their salary according to the Ministry of Railways' order. Since the increase in gold prices, the materials needed by the railway have increased more than in previous years, and military transport costs more than passenger and freight transport. Due to all these factors, the expenses this year will be 8 million yuan, and the balance of revenue and expenditure is only 3 million yuan, while the daily debt interest of 2.4 million yuan needs to be paid in gold, which requires more than 4 million yuan at the current price. Therefore, the daily debt interest this year is really difficult. As for the repair of bridges, it is estimated that it will cost more than 1.5 million yuan, which is out of the question now. It is heard that Tan will return to Qingdao tomorrow (14th), and the section chiefs will depart from Jinan tomorrow to conduct on-the-spot inspections of each station in Zhangdian, Boshan, and Jinlingzhen. (September 13th)

The Eastern Railway Bureau Establishes a Translation Office

Annual Allocation of 400,000 Yuan for Chinese-Russian Translation Affairs 55

Harbin correspondence: On the 6th of this month, the Eastern Railway Bureau received an order from the Council to establish a translation office in the bureau with an annual allocation of 400,000 yuan as regular expenses. The office will have a director and two deputy directors. The director will be Chinese and the deputy directors will be Russian. All the original translators in each department under the jurisdiction of the bureau will be transferred to the translation office to serve, specializing in translating Chinese documents into Russian and receiving and dispatching documents from all parties. After the Chinese documents are translated, they will be sent directly to the director, who will review them and then send them to each department for review and processing. The Russian documents will be received and dispatched by the office and then submitted to the director. At present, the bureau has begun to organize, and it should be established by the middle of next month. However, the way this matter is being handled is quite unsatisfactory to the Chinese directors of each department. The case of using both Chinese and Russian documents has been in dispute for many years. This spring, the Council decided to allow the bureau to reply. After several months, the bureau replied to the Council with a plan that was roughly the same. The Chinese directors were shocked when they heard the news and jointly opposed the move. The reason was that the current affairs of each department were able to proceed smoothly because of the service of these translators, who conveyed each other's opinions and avoided misunderstandings. If a translation office is specially set up in the future to concentrate the translation in one place, then the affairs of each department will not be as convenient as in the past, and it is feared that the Russian side will use the translation office to increasingly concentrate power in the director. After it was sent to the Council, it was not approved. No one has discussed this matter much in the past two months. Suddenly, an unexpected order was issued instructing them to quickly prepare for it. After the Chinese directors heard the news, they still planned to oppose it, but they were afraid that they would not be able to eliminate it. (September 8th)

The Jiangsu Provincial Propaganda Department Emphasizes Grassroots Propaganda

Order Announcing the Formation of Village and Township Mobile Propaganda Teams in Various Counties 56

The Propaganda Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Party Affairs Reorganization Committee has always paid great attention to propaganda at the grassroots level of society. Therefore, it previously organized provincial mobile propaganda teams to conduct propaganda in various counties. Since Ma Yinshui took over as the head of the department, he has paid even more attention to this point. He has specially formulated the "Organizational Plan for Village and Township Mobile Propaganda Teams in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province." This plan was passed at the 62nd meeting of the committee and has been circulated to various counties for compliance. A letter has also been sent to the provincial government requesting that it instruct all counties to provide assistance. The following is an excerpt from the "Organizational Plan for Village and Township Mobile Propaganda Teams in Various Counties": (1) Missions: 1. To expand the propaganda work of the Party during the period of political tutelage, so that the Three Principles of the People can be deeply rooted in the hearts of the people. 2. To expose the crimes of the Communist Party and all other reactionary factions in harming the country and endangering the people, and to awaken the people to jointly support the central government. 3. To investigate the activities of reactionary factions in various places. (2) Organization: 1. Each county must organize at least one propaganda team. 2. Each team shall have one leader responsible for commanding the entire team, and a number of members who, under the guidance of the leader, shall be responsible for propaganda, investigation, and other tasks. The number of members shall be determined by the county party headquarters, but there must be at least five members. 3. The personnel of the propaganda team shall be appointed by the county party headquarters from among working comrades and affiliated party members. In addition to travel expenses paid by the county party headquarters, no additional subsidies will be provided. 4. The county party headquarters should divide the county into several propaganda areas based on the geographical and transportation conditions of the county. 5. The travel expenses and propaganda expenses of the propaganda team shall be raised by the county party headquarters and may be discussed with the county government for appropriate subsidies. 6. The propaganda dates of the propaganda team shall be determined by the county party headquarters in accordance with the actual situation of the area division. (3) Work Methods: 1. Conduct disguised speeches (materials prepared by the county party headquarters). 2. Conduct individual conversations with local people separately, and carry out propaganda and investigation work as appropriate. 3. Hold mass meetings (may not be held in special circumstances). (4) Work Preparations: A. Matters for the county party headquarters to pay attention to: 1. Select personnel. 2. Raise funds. 3. Compile and print various propaganda materials and application forms (should include many pictures with simple explanations). 4. Convene propaganda team personnel for discussions, and instruct them on propaganda and investigation methods. 5. Notify the district party headquarters and district branches to be informed. 6. Notify the county government to instruct the district offices to be informed. B. Matters for the district party headquarters to pay attention to: 1. Act on behalf of preparing the food and lodging for the propaganda team (expenses borne by the propaganda team). 2. Notify all party members and the public in the district in advance. 3. Conduct preliminary investigations of local conditions for reference by the propaganda team. 4. In accordance with the propaganda team's tour dates, prepare for meetings in advance. 5. Other matters related to all assistance. C. Matters for the propaganda team to pay attention to: 1. Upon arriving at a location, immediately contact local agencies and organizations to avoid estrangement. 2. The attitude of propaganda to the people should be particularly amiable, and the method of instruction should be strictly avoided. 3. Do not create disturbances outside. 4. Do not interfere with or criticize local party and government facilities. 5. Do not entertain or accept any gifts. (5) Conclusion of Work: 1. The propaganda team must compile a report on the propaganda situation and investigation results and submit it to the propaganda department of the county party headquarters, which will then submit it to the provincial propaganda department for assessment and forward it to the county government for reference. 2. The propaganda team must prepare a detailed list of all expenses, along with receipts, and submit it to the county party headquarters for verification and cancellation.

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 57

The chief bandit of the Yangxupu gang was arrested. Qi Ajin, a notorious bandit who specialized in extorting ransoms from people in the Jiangzhuang area of Punan, was arrested last year, interrogated by the county government, and executed by firing squad. His henchmen, Lu A'er and Lu A'jun, gathered 30-40 of Qi Ajin's former subordinates, possessed more than ten guns, and called themselves the Yangxupu gang, attached to the Pudong gang in Taihu Lake. They committed crimes such as extortion, fraud, and obstruction in Yangxupu, Jiangzhuang, and other places in the southern countryside. They were not afraid of the law, and the villagers were overwhelmed by their harassment. Fearing retaliation, the villagers did not dare to report to the authorities, and the bandit's power became even more rampant. Recently, detective police from the First Branch of the Tinglin Public Security Bureau learned of the situation and reported it to Director Pan. Director Pan led the police on a night raid and arrested Lu and others. It was also discovered that after hearing that their leaders had been arrested, the remaining bandits held meetings at Wang Rongsheng's teahouse and in the home of Dr. Zhu Luxiang in Jiangzhuang. Director Pan went to arrest them again, but the bandits had already fled upon hearing the news. Only Wang Rongsheng, Zhu Hexiang's son, and the bandit Tang Awu, a total of five people, were arrested. After a brief interrogation, they were sent to Songjiang for further investigation yesterday.

The county court prosecutor was transferred. Prosecutor Lu of the county court, who had been transferred from Xiaoxian County to Songjiang, was transferred to Jiangdu County as prosecutor by the High Court before he had served for a month. The vacancy in the Songjiang court was filled by Guanghai, who took office in Songjiang the day before yesterday.

The water police captured bandits who will be escorted to the province for disposal. Du Jingwu, the leader of the first squad of the 14th team of the 3rd District of the Water Public Security Bureau, and Pei Xuan, the leader of the second squad of the guerrilla team, patrolled and searched for lake bandits in the Nankumiao area last month and successively captured Wang Heshang, Wang Xiaochen, Zheng Yousi, Liu Xueshu, and other four people. After interrogation by District Chief Gong Guoliang, the bandits confessed to robbery and kidnapping on various villages and confessed to having kidnapped the Dongshan Flying Tiger and Dalu small steamboats. He immediately reported it separately to the Three Provinces Bandit Suppression Department, the Provincial Security Office, and the Civil Affairs Department to request instructions for disposal. It is now heard that Director Li of the Provincial Security Office intends to escort the four bandits, including Wang Heshang, to the province for disposal.

Yang Xiping died strangely. Mao Jingzhi, the principal of Luowan Elementary School in Xishan, is the nephew of Mao Mujun, the district chief of the second district of the Wuxi Water Public Security Bureau. On August 7th, he accompanied his fiancée Yang Xiping and Xiping's distant nephew Yang Hangquan (25 years old, from Wujin, currently a teacher at Donghe Elementary School in Xishan), as well as Yang's concubine Zhu Tanru (38 years old) and Zhu Tanru's eldest daughter Lanzhen and second daughter Junyan to Suzhou, staying at the Hengxing Inn in Xiguanqiao. Zhu Lanzhen took the entrance exam for the [?]hai Women's School and was admitted. Junyan failed the exam for the [?]guan Sericulture School and stayed at the inn. Zhu Tanru suddenly demanded six hundred yuan in old debts from Mao Jingzhi, but Mao had no money to pay. He returned to Changzhou to raise money and originally intended to take Xiping with him, but Zhu Tanru prevented him from leaving. Mao left Xiping in Suzhou and left Suzhou alone, never to return. At that time, Xiping was already pregnant. Zhu Tanru repeatedly pressured Xiping for money at the inn. On the 10th of this month, she died due to a change in her pregnancy. Yang Hangquan pretended to be the deceased's uncle and obtained permission from the court to waive an autopsy. Yesterday (the 15th), Fang Ziqing, the patrol officer in charge of the second branch, learned of this and brought Yang Hangquan, Zhu Tanru, Zhu Junyan, and the cunning man Miaofa, who lived in the inn, to the station. Miaofa testified to the previous events. Patrol Officer Fang deemed that Yang Hangquan, the deceased's nephew, was pretending to be the deceased's uncle to request a waiver of the autopsy, which was suspicious. He brought them to the second branch for interrogation.

Zhejiang kidnappers were caught in Suzhou. A wealthy merchant from Dakiankou, Huzhou, Zhejiang, nicknamed Sanlao[?], and his junior partner were kidnapped by Zhang Yousan, Zhu Laowozi, Zhou Changhai, Zhao Guangfu, Zhang Yunbao, and other kidnappers last month. The hostages were taken to Meiyan Changyang East Beach for hiding, and a letter was sent to the hostage's family demanding a large ransom. After receiving the letter, the hostage's family entrusted someone to negotiate, and they agreed on 11,000 yuan. On the 9th of this month, they paid 5,500 yuan in advance. After Zhang[?] and others obtained the money, they had an internal dispute over the distribution of the spoils. Zhang Yunbao was shot and killed by Zhu Laowozi. Zhang Yousan obtained 1,000 yuan and fled to Suzhou. Ma Kezhong, the leader of the third squad of the 14th team of the 3rd District of the Water Public Security Bureau, learned of this and tracked him to Suzhou. On the night before last, he joined Patrol Officer Qiu Yongbiao of the 32nd branch of the Public Security Bureau to arrest him outside of the Lizhi Gate. He was immediately sent to the headquarters for verification. Yesterday (the 15th), District Chief Gong of the 3rd District of the Water Public Security Bureau sent personnel to the Public Security Bureau to pick him up and handle the case.

Wuxi 59

[?]The Court Appoints a Commissioner to Investigate the Sun Case. Former Wuxi County Magistrate Sun Zuji bailed out eight criminals before leaving office. Zhang Tong, Yang Chongyuan, Yang Zushu, and others from Wuxi believed that Sun Zuji was suspected of taking bribes to release prisoners and filed a [?] name complaint with the Provincial Government, the Civil Affairs Department, and the Jiangsu High Court. The Civil Affairs Department ordered the county to investigate the case. County Magistrate Pan sent political police to arrest and imprison the released criminals, and Liang Sanda, Gu Bohe, and others were successively apprehended. There are still three people who are being secured and ordered to surrender. The day before yesterday, Director Hu of the Civil Affairs Department specially appointed a commissioner to come to Wuxi to investigate the matter. Yesterday, President Lin of the High Court also sent judge Zheng Zhiguo to Wuxi to investigate. After getting off the train, he went directly to the county government to review the files. According to Judge Zheng, the procedures for each case seemed incomplete. At around 6:00 pm, Mr. Zheng took the car back to Suzhou to report back. Meat Industry Opposes Increasing Slaughter Tax. Wang Yun, a merchant who acknowledges the slaughter tax of the local meat industry, has been contracting the city and township meat industry slaughter tax to the Education Funding Management Office since May of the seventeenth year. It has been more than two years since. The Wuxi City Council has increased the tax amount twice. Recently, Wang Yun sent a letter to Jiang Hongzhang, the executive director of the Meat Industry Association, stating that the original amount must be increased by 20% and a loan of 2,000 yuan must be prepaid, otherwise another person will be recruited for bidding and contracting and be calculated on a per head basis. After receiving the letter, Mr. Jiang convened an emergency meeting of all colleagues at the public office the day before yesterday. All members unanimously decided to deny the increase. The reason for the opposition was that Wang Yun was an outsider and was not allowed to contract the meat industry tax. The Ministry Order had long stipulated that it should be calculated on a per head basis. According to the situation in various counties in Jiangsu Province, Wang Yun should be fully responsible. The letter was immediately sent to deny it. Yesterday, Wang Yun received a reply letter, saying that once the calculation is done on a per head basis, it will inevitably hurt feelings, and I hope to reply immediately. The meat industry has not yet replied after receiving the letter, and there is a stalemate.

Water Police Encounter Bandits on the Way to Receive Wages. Sun Rongjing, supervisor and chief accountant of the 2nd District of the Water Police, was ordered to go to the Liuhe County Finance Bureau to receive the district's wages for last month (allocated by the Financial Council's instructions). He and Patrol Officer Xiong Bin went to Zhenjiang to take a boat to Liuhe to receive a large amount of wages. On the 11th, he took the Tongchun small wheel of the Tiantai Company from Liuhe back to Zhenjiang and then transferred to Wuxi. When the wheel was passing Donggou, gunshots were heard on both sides. Before long, about twenty armed security group members came. At that time, the wheel had stopped and the gunshots had also stopped. The members of the group went straight to the boat and tied up six people who looked like military officers. Passengers were very surprised. It was only afterwards that they learned that bandits were planning to attack the wheel and the accomplices disguised themselves as passengers and got off the boat, and used the gunshots as a signal to respond from the inside and outside. Fortunately, the security group there learned of it in advance and was on strict alert. Yesterday, Chief Accountant Sun had already taken the money back to Wuxi and returned to the district office to report. Lake Bandits Discovered in Maqi Mountain. Maqi Mountain in Wujin County is adjacent to Xueyanqiao and faces Taihu Lake. There have always been bandit problems. On the morning of the day before yesterday, more than one hundred lake bandits suddenly appeared in three lake boats in the Dongniu area of the mountain. Residents were shocked and immediately reported to the Xueyanqiao Security Group, which was on strict alert and sent a special commissioner to Wuxi to report the Water Police 2nd District to send shallow-water warships to encircle and suppress the bandits in order to quell the bandit atmosphere.

Yangzhou 63

Confiscation of Copper Coin Case Three Records. The first branch of the Public Security Bureau confiscated a large number of copper coins that were being smuggled out. This newspaper has reported on this case three times. It is now heard that the county government has ordered the Public Security Bureau to investigate whether the copper coins were being smuggled out or transported to various villages to buy rice and wheat, and to report the details for verification. It is heard that the director of the Public Security Bureau, after receiving the order, ordered the branch to escort the confiscated copper coins to the bureau and sent personnel to investigate whether there were any malpractices in trafficking for profit. However, the Chamber of Commerce strongly argued that even if there were occasional copper coin trafficking exports, it would not have any impact on the livelihood of laborers and the environment of the commercial and financial markets, which is not comparable to the smuggling of imports to raise foreign prices. Moreover, the copper coins were not confiscated at wharfs or stations, so how can it be said to be smuggling? Because the two sides have different views, it has not been properly handled until today. The amount of money is indeed twenty vehicles. The so-called fifteen vehicles in yesterday's report was a transcription error.

Fengluo Ditang in Xixiang, this county, is very close, and the people were panicked when they heard the bandit alarm. Huzhou 65

A Compilation of Kidnapping Cases. Xiong Mangzi's family in Jiangheli, Daixi, Huzhou Prefecture, was well-off, so bandits coveted it. At about 9:00 pm the day before yesterday, eight or nine bandits suddenly came, holding guns and speaking in a Hakka accent. They broke down the door and entered, first tying up Xiongzi, and then entering the house to search and rob clothes and cash, with a loss of more than 200 yuan. Before leaving, they kidnapped Xiong Mangzi's 21-year-old son. Educational News

[L] Important News

Recent Situation of Tsinghua University 66

(Beijing Correspondence) Since the turmoil at Tsinghua University before the summer vacation, a year has passed easily and the autumn wind is blowing again. Although disputes have arisen frequently during the four months of summer vacation, society is very concerned about how things are going. The reporter went to Tsinghua to investigate the truth and will describe what he has learned as follows:

The Question of the President is Still Pending. Since Luo Jialun left Tsinghua, all school affairs have been discussed and handled by the school affairs meeting composed of the dean of studies, the secretary-general, the dean of the liberal arts college, the dean of the science college, and the dean of the law college. Now, the Ministry of Education has shelved Luo Jialun's resignation and feels that it is beyond its reach to deal with the aftermath. As for the North, although Qiao Wanxuan changed his policy after his last unsuccessful attempt to take over Tsinghua, it was still ineffective. There were rumors that Gu Mengyu would take over, but the general public was indifferent to it. Because the Northern authorities are busy dealing with military and political affairs, the question of Tsinghua has not yet been discussed.

The Dean of Studies is About to be Elected. The dean of studies of Tsinghua was originally filled by Wu Zhichun, the director of the Department of Political Science. Since the question of the president arose, although all affairs were decided by the school affairs meeting, Wu assumed more responsibility due to his position. Therefore, those who coveted Tsinghua said that Wu was controlling school affairs and plotting to become the president. Wu was very negative after hearing this and resigned from the position of dean of studies, and stated that he would not be responsible for matters concerning the dean of studies from August 1st. Recently, with the start of the school year approaching, the position of dean of studies must be filled, so the school affairs meeting telegraphed the Ministry of Education to ask for instructions. The reply telegram said that the faculty meeting could elect an agent. It is heard that the school affairs meeting has issued an official letter setting the morning of September 8th to convene a faculty meeting to elect an acting dean of studies and discuss school affairs. School will start on the 15th. The school affairs meeting announced that new students will report from September 8th to 9th, and a qualification test for new students will be held on the 10th. Old students will pay tuition and register from the 11th to the 13th. The opening ceremony will be held on the morning of the 15th, and classes will begin in the afternoon.

The Student Union Welcomes New Students. This year, the new students who have been admitted, including freshmen, transfer students from the second and third years, and graduate students, total about 250. They have come from afar through water and mountains. Being new to Beijing, the Student Union, according to Tsinghua's practice, organizes a new student reception committee to handle reception and welcome affairs every year. This year, the Tsinghua Summer Weekly specially printed a special issue to welcome new students, which roughly divides the current situation of Tsinghua, the question of the president, the situation of each department, and how to use the library, gymnasium, and so on.

Recent Developments in Architectural Development. The Tsinghua construction projects, including the biology building, the observatory, the library, and the student dormitory, are all planned and undertaken by the Tianjin-Keelung Construction Company. Construction began last fall and has been underway for a year. According to the contract, the biology building and the student dormitory should be completed before the start of the school year, but in fact they cannot be completed in one or two weeks and will have to be postponed for two or three weeks. The construction of the library will be completed at the end of the year, and the construction of the observatory is just beginning. It is said that the physiology building requires an expenditure of 150,000 yuan, the student dormitory 120,000 yuan, the library 260,000 yuan, and the observatory 40,000 yuan. It is also planned to start building a girls' dormitory after the start of the school year. As for the library expenditure, it was 140,000 yuan last year and has increased to 170,000 yuan this year.

Now that the social economy is bankrupt, it is not easy for national schools in Beijing to maintain the status quo, while Tsinghua has sufficient funds, a beautiful environment, and is expanding and developing. All the professors are domestic scholars, and the tuition fee is only 20 yuan per year. Some people consider Tsinghua to be a bargain, which is very reasonable. I sincerely hope that the students will make use of such a beautiful environment and the precious time that you have worked so hard to obtain. Devote yourselves to academic studies and work hard in research. Do not miss this opportunity.

Huang Pu-huan Appointed as Dean of Studies of Central University 67

Nanjing dispatch on the 15th: Ye Yuanlong, the dean of studies of Central University, was unable to take care of both his current position as associate professor in the Department of Economics and his position as dean of studies, so he resigned from his concurrent position as dean of studies and was approved to appoint Huang Pu-huan, associate professor in the School of Education of the university, as his successor.

Yunnan Dongda Changed to Provincial University 68

Nanjing dispatch on the 15th: The Yunnan Jiangfu Power Education Department stated that Dongyang University in Yunnan has been reorganized into a provincial university.

The Award and Punishment Method for Principals of All Levels of Schools to Implement Party Ideology Education is Postponed 69

The Ministry of Education previously approved the Central Executive Committee Training Department's inquiry on whether there was a need for detailed regulations on the award and punishment methods for principals of all levels of schools who can work hard to implement party ideology education, and hoped that they would review it again. After the Ministry of Education sent personnel to discuss the matter, it seemed that it could be temporarily delayed and specially replied to the Training Department. The previous official letter from your department No. 9545 stated that whether there was a need for detailed regulations on the award and punishment methods for principals of all levels of schools who implemented party ideology education should be reviewed again. The department sent Counselor Zhao Nai Chuan Kong to your department for consultation and issued it to the supervisors of your department for detailed review. Now, according to the counselor’s reply, the results of the two consultations are that the “Rules for Assessing the Research Achievements of Party Ideology by Faculty and Staff of All Levels of Schools,” the “Measures for Examining the Achievements of Party Ideology Education in All Levels of Schools,” and the “Provisional Regulations on the Study of Party Ideology by Faculty and Staff of All Levels of Schools” have been promulgated by the Central Committee and ordered by the Ministry to be followed, and the regulations have been announced and all levels of schools should implement them earnestly, and the results of the research on party ideology will be considerable over time. As for the methods for awarding and punishing principals of all levels of schools for implementing party ideology education, it seems that there is no need to make separate detailed regulations at present. After consulting with your department, it is understood that your department agreed that the methods for awarding and punishing principals of all levels of schools for implementing party ideology education can be temporarily postponed, and the letter is replied accordingly.

Jiangsu Education Department Orders Reporting of Education Statistics Forms 70

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education instructs each county education bureau: According to Article 2 of the Statistical Regulations, the statistical year shall be from August 1 of this year to July 31 of the following year according to the beginning and end of the academic year. According to Article 4, the provincial and district education statistics shall be compiled by the provincial and district education administrative agencies, and the deadline for reporting to the Ministry of Education shall not be more than four months of the following year (that is, not more than November 30 of the following year). According to Article 5, the city and county education statistics shall be compiled by the city and county education administrative agencies, and the deadline for reporting to the provincial and district education administrative agencies shall be separately stipulated by the provincial and district education administrative agencies according to the distance of the city and county routes, and so on. The above-mentioned articles have already been sent to all departments together with the explanatory notes and statistical forms by the previous Central Administrative Yuan, and they should be followed accordingly. Now, the eighteenth year has long ended, and the school education statistics for that year need to be compiled urgently. In addition to issuing separate orders, the statistical forms are issued immediately, and the director of the bureau is requested to compile them according to the format and send them to the hall before October 10 so as to compile and forward them. In addition, the statistical forms for each school (that is, Tables 1-1 to 1-5 of Form A) shall be issued by the county education bureau to each school for separate completion according to the table. The city and county school education statistical forms (that is, Tables 2-1-1 to 2-3 of Form A) shall be compiled by the county education bureau according to the tables completed by each school. Please pay attention to the important political affairs of statistics, and do not delay it slightly. This order is issued. The total number of issues: (1) Statistical Form A for each school: 3 copies of Table 1-1, 100 copies of Table 1-2, 3 copies of Table 1-3, 3 copies of Table 1-4, and 1 copy of Form B. (2) Statistical Form A for City and County School Education: 12 copies of Table 2-1-1, 20 copies of Table 2-1-2, 2 copies of Table 2-1-3, 4 copies of Table 2-1-4, 3 copies of Table 2-1-5, 1 copy of Form B, 3 copies of Table 2-1-7, 3 copies of Table 2-1-8, 3 copies of Table 2-1-9, 3 copies of Table 2-2, and 3 copies of Table 2-3.

Here is a summary of news from the preparatory office yesterday:

Continued Registration of Members: The original deadline for member registration was September 5th, but members from various locations were unable to register on time. Registration has continued in recent days. Notice of Preparatory Committee Meetings: Due to urgent matters requiring discussion, the two preparatory and hospitality committees are now scheduled to meet at 3:00 PM on the 15th of this month at the County Chamber of Commerce. All committee members have been notified to attend on time to discuss the conference topics. A compilation of topics received by the Annual Conference Preparatory Office up to the 11th is as follows: (A) Titles and Authors of Conference Papers: (1) On Removing Restrictions on Domestic Grain Trade; (2) The Future Situation of Huludao; (3) A Bird's-Eye View of Commercial Conditions and Navigation in the Yangtze River Basin. All three are by Li Yunliang. (4) A Study of the Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement, by Jia Shiyi. (5) Research on Investment, by Zhang Yuanjie. (6) Fluid Economics. (7) From the Materialist Conception of History to the New Idealist Conception of History. Both by Li Quanshi. (8) On Accounting Subjects, by Zhou Yiyun. (9) Fiscal Problems, by □ Xiu Jia. (10) The Influence of Foreign Banks in China. (11) Improvement of the Financial Supervision System. Both by Zong Xianjun. (B) Topics for Open Discussion at the Annual Conference: (1) The Gold and Silver Question, proposed by the Quarterly Journal Society. (2) Future Provincial Finances, proposed by the Hangzhou Branch.

Proposals for the Society's Business Meeting: (1) The Society should add sponsoring members (Proposed by the Board of Directors). (2) Membership qualifications should be restrictive. Those without economic writings or contributions to economic undertakings should not be admitted to the Society (Proposed by the Board of Directors). (3) The Society should promote the establishment of branches, and members should be divided into groups to study economic problems in order to strengthen unity and promote academic development. (4) It is recommended that the government promptly enact banking regulations to consolidate the national financial organization (Both of the above two proposals were made by Zhu Binyuan). (5) Members should strive for the independence of economic science and the Sinicization of economic books. (6) The Society's funds should be allocated primarily to publishing expenses (Both of the above two proposals were made by Li Quanshi). (7) When major economic problems occur in society, the Society should hold more lectures in major ports and publish articles for social reference (Proposed by Ma Chonggan). Lecture Topics for the Annual Conference: Speakers and topics for the annual conference: Shao Yuanchong, agricultural policy; He Deqiu, remedies for bank failures; Li Yunliang, from Wuxi industry to the Chinese economy or infringed Chinese navigation rights; Zhu Qinglai, Communism and the Doctrine of Loyalty and Forgiveness.

Minutes of the County Bureau of Education's Bureau Affairs Meeting 75

The Shanghai County Bureau of Education held its 166th Bureau Affairs Meeting yesterday morning after the weekly memorial service for the Prime Minister. All staff members were present, with Director Shi presiding and Pan Sansheng recording. After the customary formalities, the report of matters was briefly presented, and then the discussion of motions began: (1) A motion to nominate two members of the Bureau's Economic Audit Committee for this term was passed, nominating Zhu Hange and Niu Zhiyi as members of the committee. (2) A motion regarding the date for convening the Economic Audit Committee was passed, deciding that it would be held at 1:00 PM on September 28th. (3) A motion to investigate private schools was passed, resolving to summarize the results of the district principals' meetings and determine the method as follows: (A) The investigation form shall be drafted by the School Education Section. (B) The investigation method shall be that the Bureau orders each school to investigate within its respective school district and report by the end of October. (4) A motion from the Sixth District Principals' Association requesting postponement of tuition fee deductions was resolved, stating that it concerned budgeted regular income and could not be approved. (5) A letter from the Second District Office requesting allocation of surplus start-up funds for the Tangmin School □ was resolved, stating that since the start-up funds had already been diverted by the District Office, it was currently impossible to supplement them, and the request could not be approved. (6) A motion from Zhenxin Primary School requesting continued temporary funding was resolved, stating that the Bureau's entire budget had already been determined, and this additional request could not be approved. (7) A letter from the Fourth District Office forwarding a request from the Haihui Primary School for additional teaching assistants was resolved, stating that it violated Provincial Order No. 855 and could not be approved. (8) A motion regarding the editing outline of the 18th-year annual report was resolved, nominating Niu Zhiyi and Lin Weiwen to review it before submitting it to the next meeting for discussion. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

(8) Singing of the mourning song. (9) Delivery of eulogies. (10) Announcement of memorial methods. (11) Family members' reply. (12) Playing of mourning music. (13) Adjournment. The discussion on the Yijiao Memorial District methods continued. Pu Xieying reported that there are more than 2,100 school-age children in Liuhang, of whom more than 700 have already enrolled. The original ten schools require more than 6,000 yuan in annual funding. Promoting universal education can start by adding levels. Each additional level costs 150 yuan in start-up fees and 316 yuan in recurring expenses. Adding a school costs 250 yuan in start-up fees and 348 yuan in recurring expenses. Currently, 1,455 children in Liuhang Township are not enrolled. Assuming 50 people per level, it is estimated that about□ 29 levels or 2 schools and 27 levels will be added to reach the popularization period. The plans for the three-year popularization period and the five-year popularization period are listed in separate tables. Huang Renzhi reported that Mr. Yuan advocated setting up distribution schools that integrate moral education into agriculture and industry to prevent students from dropping out. This proposal has been very effective. Wu Shiqiao reported on the Baoshan memorial methods: (1) The family members have already agreed to the public burial site, and the location is being planned. (2) The private sanctuary is currently planned to have three locations, which will be decided by the public at the memorial service. Zheng Xigu reported that he is willing to establish a memorial碑 at Shanghai Middle School to perpetuate his memory.

Laoda Intensifies Students' Production Work

Increasing the Work Hours of Students at All Levels and Assigning Work Types According to Department 78

The National Labor University has formulated a new plan for production work this semester. The work hours will be 12 to 18.5 hours per week. The types of work will be assigned according to the nature of each college and department, with the aim of complementing what is learned in work. For example, the □ Art Department of the Agricultural College will plant vegetables and flowers; the Agricultural Science Department will plant rice, wheat, and cotton; the Agricultural Chemistry Department will manufacture agricultural products; the Engineering College will engage in ironwork, woodwork, and car repair; and the Social College will engage in printing work, undertaking the printing of the school's weekly and other kinds of printed materials. The income and expenditure of the above work products will be submitted by each college to the accounting department for comprehensive review. The technical and supervisory aspects will be □ the responsibility of the deans, directors, and instructors of each college.

Free Talk

A Laughing Matter 87

— Hai Ke

Dentist (to his neighbor's child): Your father is really a miser. He owns a shoe store and can make shoes himself. Why does he always make you wear broken shoes?

Son of the shoe worker: That's not the point. For example, you are a dentist, so why does your little brother only have one tooth?

Girl A: I recently got a lover. Every time we meet, he always praises me endlessly, saying how beautiful and lively I am. I will definitely marry him in the future.

Girl B: He started out by telling lies and deceiving you. Do you still want to grow old with him?

Father: Child, why do you fail every exam and never bring back good grades?

Son: Because the good grades were all snatched away by other classmates. I just have to make do with what's left.

A: It wasn't easy for me to get to this high and mighty position. I don't need to hide it from you, my old friend. I was originally just a barefoot child.

B: What's so rare about that? When I first came out of my mother's womb, I was also barefoot and didn't wear shoes.

Eulogy to Juan Zhi 88

— Tao Zaidong

The elderly Yu Juanzhi of Changsha, a recluse in Shanghai, passed away on the 17th of this month at the age of seventy-seven. Alas! The gentleman was appointed to the Ministry of Works as a tribute scholar and changed to Prefect, serving in Hubei, successively holding positions in Jingzhou, Hanyang, and Wuchang. Wherever he went, officials feared him and the people cherished him. His reputation spread far and wide. He □ rose to the position of Jingyi Shi Xiangyang Dao, with the expectation of being a regional official. When Jiang Zhaotang of Nanchang County was murdered, he negotiated the case with reason and fought for it, supported by public opinion. This is what is now called strong diplomacy. He disobeyed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and □ had his rank removed and left his job. After a long time, Minister of Law Dai Wenjian awarded him the position of Left Counselor of the Ministry of Law, but he did not take office. When the party disaster occurred, he was condemned and expelled in accordance with the wishes of Privy Councilor Qu Wenshen. He both embraced the loyalty of Huai Sha and experienced the sorrow of Gaoyu's loss of the country. He resigned himself to spending his old age in a poor rural area, but due to frequent bandit troubles, he hurriedly opened up land to seek refuge in the concession, which was not his original intention. The gentleman loved talent like Pang Shiyuan, encouraging later generations, often exaggerating the truth. As a junior relative, I was fortunate to receive his knowledge early, but I have no learning, no official career, and white hair on my temples after surviving the tiger's mouth. It has already deserted Lu Shi's village and does not dance with Yang Gong's cranes. I have exhausted my strength to come to Shanghai, indulging in literature and wine, and relatives' words are also very pleasing. However, the flames of war have continued for years, thorns and thorns are everywhere, the day is late and the road is far, what kind of world is this? Heaven's will and human affairs can be a source of sadness and heartache. How can an elegy be completed? His couplet says: His heart hangs in the sky, his loyalty shines brightly, his meritorious name is a trivial matter in the annals of time, his articles are praised in the north, his eyes are full of vicissitudes, his feelings are vast and touching, and one day, the hill collapses, and someone cries sadly over the west continent.

The Novel Fanatic of Today 89

— Lü Bing

I recently read in the newspaper that two students in Wuxi were so fascinated by martial arts novels that they left without saying goodbye, intending to travel around and find a teacher. Also, this month's Zi Lin Xi Bao also reported that a twelve-year-old Russian child, Fan Zige Fusi, was so fond of reading nautical novels that he secretly took two other Russian children on a sampan, intending to float to Qingdao. Fortunately, they were found by their family the next day and taken back. The magic of novels is so great that it cannot but be shocking. However, the above two stories all came from the actions of young children, and it may be considered that they have simple minds and are not worth mentioning. However, when I turned to Western magazines, I found that even older writers and travelers were also fascinated by novels and tried to experience the realm of the ancients. The matter is quite bizarre, so I translated it to provide a smile.

It is not easy to do the business of Robinson Crusoe in the present century, but there is indeed a second Robinson Crusoe in the world today. Who is he? It is the Englishman Harry Burden. Mr. Harry is good at literature and loves to travel. He once set sail and arrived at Dupanggu Island, living in a cave for a month. All the clothes were imitated from Robinson Crusoe's original ones, and his companions were a parrot, a hound, and a goat. Later, he found a native on the island, and because the date he met him was a Thursday, he called him Thursday. He has nothing to do all day, so he fells large trees on the island, hollows them out, and makes canoes for fishing and hunting. However, Robinson Crusoe's original purpose was to leave the island and return to his country, but he had no such thoughts. If the magazine's record is very accurate, then Mr. Harry is truly worthy of being an outstanding member of the novel fanatic.

Small Recipe 90

— Yang Yixiao

Lotus Seed Porridge: Fresh lotus pods are shelled, peeled, and the hearts removed, then cooked into porridge with fragrant japonica rice in a sand pot. It is exceptionally clear and fragrant.

Chestnut Soup: Chestnuts are shelled, peeled, and cut in half, then fried in a pot until crispy. Then add osmanthus honey and a little white sugar. It is fragrant and sweet, and the taste is no different from real osmanthus chestnut.

Persimmon Steamed Balls: Peel the persimmons and mash them in a stone mortar with a pestle. Mix with glutinous rice flour and knead into balls. For the salty version, use dried □ vegetables, shrimp, and meat filling. For the sweet version, use a filling of dried fruit, bean paste, and sugar. The balls are lined with bamboo leaves and arranged in a steamer to steam. It is even sweeter and more delicious than dry pumpkin steamed balls.

New Things in Pear Garden, Spring in Beijing 91

— Plum Blossom Pavilion Master

Cheng Yanqiu has already agreed with the Grand Theatre to leave for the South after the Mid-Autumn Festival. Before leaving Beijing, he is still performing at the Harbin Theatre. The actors in the same class include Guan Dayuan, Hao Shoushen, and Zhou Rui'an. It was previously said that Cheng would go to Dalian, but according to a letter from a Beijing friend, this statement has been refuted.

Li Huiqin, who came to Shanghai with Li Guifen last year, has now invited Wang Youchen and Shang Heyu to form a separate class, first at Zhonghe and now moving to Kaiming.

Among the Kun roles in Beijing, in addition to the already famous Xue Yanyun and Xin Yanqiu, the most popular and artistically refined is Du Liyun, a female disciple of Wang Yaoqing. Miscellaneous Talks on Phonographs and Records 92

— Rong Bo

I have been immersed in records for nearly twenty years. Whenever I meet friends, they ask me about my interest in records. Some may even regard me as an experienced guide. If there are matters of purchasing phonographs or records, they must ask me to decide what to buy. Initially, I felt overwhelmed by the booming record industry and the profusion of new releases, making it hard to choose. However, I have a peculiar fondness for this, and have spent almost half my life on it. Therefore, I have a considerable understanding of the quality of various records.

The effort put into recording has brought about a special kind of progress and given us excellent news. My interest in records has grown even stronger. However, if the recording of electric sound records is poorly arranged, or if the technician is unskilled, the result can be unbearable. Fortunately, this is rare. However, it is common for records to have different sound levels. First Company records have different levels of bass, so needles come in three types: high, medium, and low, making it easier for phonograph owners to choose.

Regarding phonographs, from my perspective, if financially possible, it's best to buy the highest quality one. The beautiful sound it produces can dispel worries and be even better than the original singer. Through my experience over the years and research with friends, it seems that the Brunswick sound head provides the most accurate sound. Next would be Victor. The machine should also be large (or custom-made, if you can get the sound head, it will be cheaper than imported ones). A larger sound gate is also necessary. The minimum diameter of the sound gate should be eight inches, and larger is better. The internal sound horn should not be made of metal, otherwise the beauty of the singer's flesh and blood voice will be lost. The price of a custom-made floor phonograph is only about two hundred yuan. If you buy an imported one, due to the high price of gold, even a machine with a lid but no legs will cost around two hundred yuan.

Regarding record quality, I find the recently released "Kaiming" records satisfactory. Not only is the sound clear and loud—some complain it's too loud, but it sounds wonderful with a fine needle—but the quality is far superior to others. The selection of dramas is also very sophisticated. The roles are well-organized, and there are many complete dramas with dialogues and singing. The sound levels of each record are also consistent, which is commendable.

The 300-Year-Old Man in America 93

— Wang Jin

The idea of immortality is promoted by alchemists, recorded in unofficial histories, and believed by women and children. Scholars, however, dismiss it as superstition. The "Shen Bao" reported a few years ago that an old man in Sichuan was over two hundred years old, which was considered a marvel. Yesterday, I heard that Liu Xing, the former commander of the Eighth Army, sent a letter to his brother from New York, saying that there was a 297-year-old man in America. Is there really such a thing as immortality? Here is a summary of the letter:

"On the ninth day after I (Liu Xing) arrived in New York, I took a plane to a certain place (I forgot the name). Due to heavy fog, we landed in a village, which translates to 'Spring Valley.'"

"I found this village to be a paradise compared to the noisy days and nights of New York. I was drawn to its tranquility and stayed for a week. The pilot flew back the same day. There, I met an old man who claimed to be 297 years old. Besides one great-great-grandchild, he has no relatives. He has the face of a child, white hair, and walks very fast. When asked how he achieved such longevity, he replied: 'I do not eat, drink, sleep, or laugh at the wrong time. I do not argue with people or go against nature. I adapt to circumstances, and I do not worry or fret.' The village has over a hundred residents, mostly natives. They are all kind and friendly. There is a stream over two hundred li long. I took a canoe to the stream's exit and then took a boat back to New York. The village is about a thousand miles from New York."

The above letter was dictated by my friend Mr. Deng. I heard that the entire letter was about three thousand words long. - Wang Jin

News from the Publishing Industry: The "Shuang Shuang Hu Die" (Paired Butterflies) songbook is the most popular song of modern times. All girls' schools have adopted it as a textbook. The Bei Kai Company has specially produced it into a record that is very popular. The songbook is sold for only two jiao. The Wenming Dadong Bookstore and the Hudie Song and Dance Club in Jiu'an Lane, Huangjiaque Road, also have collections for sale.

Travels in Nanyang (50) 94

— Linghua

On the 12th, I arrived at Penang Island. The mountain I saw resembled the Lion Mountain in Nanjing and the Gold Mountain, unlike the flat hills of Singapore. Upon landing, I met the secretary of the former Tang Dynasty consul to Penang, Pei Yuan (courtesy name Shuyuan), who has a family reputation for calligraphy and painting and is currently running a Ya Nan Normal School. Upon arriving in Penang, I stayed at the Guanyin Temple on Cheshui Street. The temple monk, Master Baoling, treated me very kindly. That evening, Dr. Xu Xiaoshan invited guests such as Dai Zhiting and Dai Peiyuan to a banquet at the foot of Kek Lok Si Temple. The scenery of Kek Lok Si is similar to the Western Hills of Beijing. We sat until 8 pm, and it already felt cool, unlike the heat of Singapore. The climate here is cooler and fresher. Doctor Xu is skilled in poetry and medicine and earns a thousand yuan per month.

On the morning of the 13th, I visited the Guanyin Pavilion and the Guangtong Master. The master is the honorary president of the Buddhist Studies Society. I was invited to dinner there. After dinner, I visited the research society, which had about a hundred male and female members who were worshiping, similar to the Japanese walking barefoot around the courtyard chanting Buddhist scriptures. I discussed Buddhism with the president, Mr. Li, and Mr. Yang in English. Generally speaking, the Nanyang region practices Theravada Buddhism. I received a letter from my friend Da Xiyin in Siam, who said that people who practice Theravada Buddhism have fewer desires and are content, so unrest does not arise. This is especially true of those who have become monks. If Theravada Buddhism becomes widespread, it may also put an end to human strife and killing.

On the 15th, Mr. Dai Shuyuan visited and invited me to the seaside to watch men and women swimming. Western women swim in the sea with men. Their physiques are truly strong and active. Ancient Chinese books also discussed women bathing. For example, the "Book of Songs" states that "Heaven commanded the dark bird to descend and give birth to Shang." There was a woman named E'e who was about to have a child. The "Historical Records" say that Yin Qi's mother, Jian Di, was the daughter of the E'e clan. Three women were bathing when they saw a dark bird's egg and swallowed it, giving birth to Qi. The "Qing Donghua Records" say that the ancestor of the Aisin Gioro clan also swallowed a bird's egg while his grandmother was bathing. These are all imitations of Chinese books that are attributed to divine events. However, in fact, the women of the three northeastern provinces still bathe in the river to this day. In Guangdong and Guangxi, I have seen many female boatmen, some as young as seven or eight, learning to swim in the river. North of the Huai River and within the Great Wall, almost no women can bathe in the river. On the other hand, the ancient Roman education system had women learning to swim. This shows what their customs were like. Today, at the narrowest point of the cape between England and France, called the Dover Strait, no man can swim across. However, a certain woman has swum across the cape, proving that the physical fitness of women in modern times is improving and they have the ability to surpass men. Also, recently, a 21-year-old British woman flew a plane to Nanyang, saying she would make a 12,000-mile flight.

Eastern Tour Correspondence (18) 95

— Wu Xiaohou

South of the concert hall is a large sports ground, about 7,000 tsubo in size, equipped for various large gatherings. Along the west side of the ground is the Rhododendron Hill, about 1,000 tsubo in size. This is where the landscaping began. It is the Rhododendron Garden of Okubo. It is evenly planted with autumn grass and Kerria japonica, among other things. Several elegant walking paths and a pavilion on a small hill make this one of the most refined parts of the park. To the west of the Rhododendron Garden is a Western-style cloud-shaped pond with an azalea facing the pond. From the front, there is a crane fountain. There are elegant bridges and wisteria trellises over the moat. Nearby are many exotic flowers, rare herbs, and ancient trees, creating scenes that never fade throughout the four seasons. From a positional point of view, it is located in the center of the garden and is constantly visited by people walking with canes. The northeast area of the concert hall, the area from the main gate through the music gate to the tower gate, is often used by the public. In the center of this area is a Western-style flower bed of about 1,000 tsubo, planted with various Western flowers and plants, including mixed flower beds or plantings of Liatris spicata and Stachys byzantina, with red flowers and purple herbs competing for glory in all seasons. To the southeast of the flower bed is the old Hibi Valley moat and stone ramparts, intended to preserve the old Japanese garden. There is a wild crane raised on the Horai Island in the pond, and other ponds are stocked with ducks, geese, mandarin ducks, and other waterfowl that lazily play and sleep among the lotus and reeds. The stone ramparts are the most desolate place in the garden and also a great place for viewing. To the northwest of the flower bed is a place for planting flowers and trees, as well as sample trees. The northwest area of the garden, from the Sakura Gate to the Kasumi Gate, has a grassland of 4,000 tsubo. In the center are three tennis courts. On the north side are three hills 75.3 meters high, inside which are a bird-feeding ground, a youth sports ground, a children's playground, and animal houses. The southwest corner of the garden, from the Kasumi Gate to the Saiwai Gate, has a forest of various trees. Recently, a large outdoor theater and a new concert hall for Western and Eastern music have been built inside. In addition to music, this place provides other public entertainment and is also planned for use for social education. There are more than 3,200 seats and it can accommodate 5,000 people. To the south of this forest area, the small triangular area from Saiwai Gate to the Saiwai Gate is planted with various trees, creating a very beautiful forest. There is a library inside. In the garden, the Matsumoto Building, the Mitsuhashi Pavilion, the Kirin Pavilion, and the Takayanagi Pavilion, among other tea and coffee shops, provide places to rest.

Investigation of Silver and Foreign Currency Reserves in Shanghai

Silver 107.04 Million Taels, Foreign Currency 148.24 Million Big Bars 2728 Bars 99

This year, the financial situation in Shanghai has been affected by cheap silver, and there has been no opportunity for a turnaround for a long time. As a result of the current silver flooding, the government has banned imports, but this has ultimately failed to restore the original state of the market. Instead, the mint is now opening its furnaces to cast coins, resulting in a shortage of raw materials. An investigation of the reserves in Shanghai in the first half of the year shows that the big bar reserves were always at 6-7,000. The Chinese banks have less than 400, while the 2,000+ are in the vaults of foreign banks. Although the current silver reserves are relatively large, they actually supply the demand for the market to circulate and for the mint to use as raw materials. The foreign currency reserves are mostly banknote reserves for the various banks, and the amount circulating on the market is purely negligible, and I do not expect the residual amount to be so small either (48 million yuan). Here is a detailed list of the deposit amounts in the warehouses of the various banks and qianzhuang (units of silver and foreign currency: 10,000; units of big bars: bars)

Yarn and Flower Situation Continues to Slacken 101

The yarn market experienced a morning drop followed by an afternoon rise, but the overall situation remains unfavorable. This is because the existing stock is too substantial and sales are sluggish. Therefore, sellers are maintaining a calm attitude. Additionally, the global economic situation is weak, leading to softened sentiment. However, certain manufacturers remain bullish and continue to increase their holdings, purchasing at the limit price of 9 liang for this month. Fundamentally, raising prices may halt spot sales and lead to inventory accumulation, making it difficult to reduce stock. Thus, with weak demand, the future outlook is not optimistic. It is feared that the current yarn market price may experience a significant drop, as it is too high compared to future yarn prices. Recent daily declines in Japanese yarn prices are said to be gaining momentum.

The Raw Cotton Market: Morning Decline, Afternoon Stability. The raw cotton market opened in the morning with a negative environment, characterized by bleak American cotton and news that a raw cotton merchant from Wuhu had closed his 6,000-piece contract with great pain due to margin call issues. Market sentiment eased further, with prices for each month falling by 0.012 to 0.023 taels. In the afternoon, the old bullish investors from Hengda Factory bought heavily at the limit price of 9 taels in September, stirring the market and causing slight gains in prices for each month, ranging from 0.011 to 0.069 taels. The total trading volume for the day was 28,350 bales. Sales included 2,400 bales of Hanfeng, 1,400 bales of Yongchang, 1,650 bales of Xincheng, 1,200 bales of Lichang, 1,005 bales of Shenxin, 950 bales of Tianchang, and 400 to 600 bales of others. Purchases included 1,150 bales of Da Ji, 1,150 bales of Yuantai, 1,500 bales of Yikang, 900 bales of Heshen, 950 bales of Shen Ji, 800 bales of Yongfeng, and 400 to 700 bales of others. The closing prices of the raw cotton market are recorded on the left.

Cotton Market Lifeless 102

The cotton market was lifeless this morning due to the bleak situation in American cotton, stagnant actual demand, weak sentiment, and the decline in the yarn market, leading most factories to refrain from purchasing. However, domestic merchants, noting the poor harvests in the Jiangsu and Zhejiang areas, bought a significant amount of cotton. Additionally, hand-to-mouth buyers also purchased 20,000 dan. It is said that some, seeing the unfavorable overall situation, have already exited the market. If domestic merchants and hand-to-mouth buyers start to sell off, there may be another significant drop in the market. How the raw cotton merchant faction will proceed depends on demand and weather conditions.

Raw Cotton Market Slightly Better in the Afternoon. The raw cotton market opened in the morning in a rather panicked state. As foreign cotton was not selling, retail investors sold off, causing drops of 0.035 to 0.04 taels across the board. In the afternoon, with a slight rise in the yarn market and unfavorable weather, retail investors bought in, causing a rebound of 0.015 to 0.02 taels across all months. Total trading volume for the day was 53,300 dan. Sales included 3,000 dan of Lichang, 1,900 dan of Yukang, 1,000 dan of Yongfeng, 1,100 dan of Shenyu, 1,400 dan of Tianchang, and 1,100 to 1,400 dan of others. Purchases included 2,400 dan of Jinfeng, 4,100 dan of Tianlong, 2,100 dan of Zhenda, and 1,400 to 1,200 dan of others. The closing prices of the raw cotton market are recorded on the left.
