Grain and Rice Market: River Down Rice – Japonica Firm, Indica Weak. 105

Yesterday in Zhabei, the source of various arrivals varied in quantity, and sales were also mixed between brisk and sluggish. Broken white rice was scarce and sales were robust, leading to a firm market. Premium grades opened at 20.075 yuan. Arrivals of West New Japonica were strong, estimated at over 300 shi, with higher grades at 20.0 yuan and lower grades at 19.5 yuan. East New Japonica arrivals were scarce, and factory stocks were gradually depleting, leading merchants to hoard goods, causing a price increase of 0.5 yuan. The high opening price was 20.0 yuan. New Yangjian rice fell by about 0.2 yuan. Arrivals of rice from inland areas at the wharf saw weak buying interest, and the market opened at only 14.8 yuan. New Kejian rice was also weak, falling by about 0.2-0.3 yuan. Rice from various areas along the Yangtze River in Southern Anhui and Eastern Jiangxi continued to arrive in Shanghai, leading to a continued weakening of the market by about 0.2-0.3 yuan. Arrivals of White Yuan rice were also limited, and sales in the local market were relatively brisk, thus the market presented a stable appearance. Top grades once again approached the 19 yuan level.

Supplies from the Shanghai South River were scarce from only a few dealers, and market activity was extremely calm. Sources of broken inland japonica rice were very limited, causing sellers to pressure sales and hindering trading activity, leading to a slightly firm market. The trend for Southern paddy rice was also stable, with high-priced goods at 21 yuan, but these were all small-scale transactions. The market for East New Japonica rice reported shortages, leading to few transactions. A small amount of Yangjian rice arrived in Shanghai, but sales were not brisk, with high-priced goods selling at around 14 yuan, slightly weaker by about 0.1 yuan compared to the previous day.

Notice: The price evaluation association established by the Northern City Social Bureau will only be dissolved after rice prices on all markets reach 10 yuan.

Flour Market's Recent Steepest Decline 106

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning and afternoon, the market for all months showed a consistent downward trend, especially for the current month. This is because the bulls in the current month mostly relied on the manufacturers' intentions. Now it is known that although the manufacturers' buy orders have been gradually removed by the raw cotton traders by 300,000 to 400,000 bales, it is rumored that a certain factory, feeling that the environment is unfavorable, intends to completely abandon the buy orders that were scheduled to be removed. Therefore, the opening price immediately fell. Subsequently, outside speculators, having lost their support, also aggressively sold out their positions, so the lowest price once fell to 2.04475 taels, a sharp drop of 0.055 taels compared to the previous week's closing price. October fell to 1.041 taels, and the other months also fell by 0.02-0.03 taels. By the second session in the afternoon, rumors spread that spot purchases could be made again this month, so sentiment slightly recovered and distant months also showed slight improvement. However, if the price of foreign wheat remains low, the outlook is still uncertain. As a result, the current month fell by 0.0375 taels, October fell by 0.0325 taels, November fell by 0.0175 taels, December fell by 0.02 taels, January fell by 0.0125 taels, and February fell by 0.01 tael.

Wheat Futures Plunge by 0.06-0.07 Taels 107

Foreign Wheat Continues to Fall, Bulls Exit

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning and afternoon, the plunge in all months was even more chaotic and reached its extreme. The price of foreign wheat continued to fall by about 0.3-0.4 yuan. The bullish raw cotton merchants, since the manufacturers had already sold foreign wheat, would naturally reject domestic wheat even more in the future, so the raw cotton traders' sell-off was extremely robust. Temporary speculative shorts also continuously pressured the market, so the lowest price for September, October, and November fell by a huge 0.11-0.12 taels compared to the previous week. Distant months generally fell by 0.07-0.08 taels. However, between the second and third sessions, manufacturers covering their shorts competed to cover their positions, causing a rebound of 0.04-0.05 taels for near months, and a slight rebound for distant months. As a result, September fell by 0.06 taels compared to the previous week, October fell by 0.07 taels, November fell by 0.06 taels, and December to February fell by 0.04 taels. Spot Wheat Market: As benchmark prices have plummeted, factories are even less interested in inquiring about prices.

North-South Goods: New Quanzhou Bullets and Rounds Opened Yesterday 108

Top-Grade Prices at 30 Taels; Lower Grades Extremely Cheap

The first batch of over 3,000 boxes of Quanzhou Bullets and Rounds arrived recently on the Huaheng Wheel. Due to the late arrival in Shanghai, it coincided with the time when Tong'an Rounds prices were at their lowest. Moreover, the goods were newly arrived, and most were damp and soft and could not be stored for long. With nothing to defend and no price to report, the dealers had no choice but to sell at market prices, leading to extremely chaotic market prices. Yesterday, the entire batch was sold. Top-grade goods opened at 30 taels, with subsequent grades cheaper by 1-2 taels, down to 2-3 taels. Middle-grade goods were priced at 22-23 taels down to 20 taels, and the lowest grade was not above 10 taels. The cheapness of the lower grades was unprecedented in recent years, as the trading floor was extremely sluggish.

Fine Twill Piece Goods Selling Strongly 109

Prices for Other Goods Have Softened

Recently, the local cotton cloth market has been affected by the frequent drops in flower and yarn prices, coupled with sluggish actual sales, leading to a gradual decline. Yesterday, fine cloth was down by about 0.05 yuan, and gray cloth also softened. However, fine twill remains firm and selling strongly due to a lack of spot goods. Yesterday, transactions in the local market and by Ningbo and other guilds totaled over 100 pieces, with Yanghe selling for 7.25 taels, Blue Double Fish for 6.875 taels, Butterfly Ball for 6.725 taels, and 13-pound coarse cloth purchased by raw cotton traders for over 50 pieces, with Double Eagle selling for 5.95 taels, Horse Dog for 5.9 taels, and Double Horse for 5.85 taels. Fine cloth saw the sharpest decline in Blue Chicken, selling for 6.65 taels, and Blue Flying Fish also softened, selling for 7.15 taels yesterday.

The trend for Eastern and Western piece goods is softening, especially for Eastern goods, which have seen a steeper decline. This is largely because the previous price increases were too excessive, making it difficult for those in need to commit. Moreover, those holding goods, seeing the rising market prices, are all seeking to sell, leading to an oversupply. With actual sales stagnant, the market suddenly became depressed. Yesterday, Middle Flower Velvet was down by 0.025 to 0.05 yuan, Chicken Coop selling for 0.1975 yuan, White Peony for 0.195 yuan, Straight Tribute Satin down by 0.025 yuan, Flying Horse and Magpie Bridge Meeting both opening at 0.28 yuan, and Banana Leaf Title Book at 0.275 yuan. However, Fine Geji remains firm, with Treasure Ball at 0.31 yuan and Lakeside Pavilion at 0.27 yuan, likely due to a shortage of spot goods. Western goods saw no major changes, and Releasing Carp Straight Tribute Serge bucked the trend and opened at 0.245 yuan yesterday.

Local News

Song Ziwen Indicates That Abolishing Likin May Be Postponed 116

Inspection of Shandong's Tax Revenue Shows Good Results

New Tariff Rules May Be Announced Before National Day

Minister of Finance Song Ziwen went to Qingdao and then to Jinan to inspect the financial and tax revenue situation in Shandong Province. He returned to Shanghai by the Changchun Maru at 3 PM on the 14th. He went to the Central Bank's Ministry of Finance office yesterday morning to work. This reporter made a special trip to meet him. According to Mr. Song, he was quite satisfied with this trip to Shandong to inspect the financial and tax revenue situation. The income from national taxes such as tobacco and alcohol was quite abundant. When the Jin army was defeated, it was very hasty, so only 300,000 yuan was raised locally from the banking community in Jinan. Other taxes were not transferred at all. Now that Shandong's tax revenue has been sorted out, it should be even more considerable. When he passed through Qingdao, he met with Mayor Hu Ruoyu, but he did not discuss political issues. When asked about the abolition of likin and the new import tariff rules, Mr. Song said that the Ministry of Finance had made thorough preparations for the abolition of likin, and the provinces also had detailed reports to the Ministry. However, due to the war, it was slightly difficult. The Ministry of Finance hopes to implement it as scheduled on Double Ten Day, but if it is absolutely necessary, it can only be postponed slightly. As for the national new tariff rules, the Ministry of Finance has submitted them to the Legislative Yuan, which has been sent to the Finance Committee for review. It is expected that the new tariff rules will be announced before National Day. The new tariff rules and the abolition of likin cannot be discussed together. Whether or not the abolition of likin is implemented has no relationship to the implementation of the new tariff rules. In short, if the military situation ends early, there will definitely be a solution to the financial situation, etc.

Shanghai-Sichuan Aviation Suffers Setback 117

Jiujiang Aircraft Test Flight to Yichang

Suddenly Returned to Hankou Yesterday

The China Aviation Corporation is preparing for the official flight from Shanghai to Hankou, extending to the Chongqing line, at the beginning of next month. Last Friday, the chief and deputy directors of the company's air navigation team, Smith and Nie Kaiyi, flew the Jiujiang aircraft for a test flight to Chongqing, as reported in detail in previous newspapers. According to the original plan, the Jiujiang aircraft could have arrived in Chongqing yesterday. However, according to a telegram received by the local aviation company from Hankou yesterday, the Jiujiang test flight had safely arrived in Yichang the day before and stayed overnight. They were just about to continue flying to Wanxian and Chongqing, when they suddenly received a radio message from a private source in Chongqing stating that Liu Xiang's side had not yet received a formal telegram informing them of the test flight to Chongqing, and that the local authorities there had not been properly contacted, so a rash flight might cause misunderstandings. Nie Kaiyi and others then decided to fly the original aircraft back to Hankou from Yichang for the time being and then decide whether to advance or retreat. According to the telegram obtained by the local aviation company, it was only known that the Jiujiang aircraft arrived in Hankou at 11 AM yesterday. As of 4 PM yesterday, there had been no further telegram reports from Hankou as to whether it would continue to fly back to Shanghai. According to what the aviation company knows, before the test flight, Nie Kaiyi had already telegraphed the Wuhan Commander-in-Chief and Sichuan Commander-in-Chief Liu, in his personal capacity, about the Shanghai-Chongqing air route. Liu had replied in support and said that the original Chongqing airfield could be borrowed. The reason for the setback in the middle of the flight may be that the telegram sent by the Ministry of Transportation to Chongqing had not yet been received, causing a misunderstanding. The local aviation company is now trying to contact Liu in Sichuan again, and will continue the test flight as soon as a satisfactory result is obtained. Whether the official opening of the Shanghai-Chongqing air route, originally scheduled for the beginning of next month, will be affected by this depends on the extent of the negotiations.

Execution of Jinliyuan Wharf Case Postponed Again

Director Li Consults with Staff for Days 118

Regarding the Jinliyuan Wharf case of the China Merchants Bureau, the Sandetang side has not yet received a reply from the Paris headquarters regarding the land price for the purchase of a portion of the wharf, and the deadline for reconciliation given by the French Public Concession last time has expired yesterday. Lawyer Gao Shuo and China Merchants Bureau Director Cai have sent letters to the French Consul General, the French Public Concession, and Sandetang, respectively, stating that the responsibility for the delay should be borne by the other party. It is reported that the French Consul General has expressed his willingness to allow Lawyer Gao Shuo, Deputy Director Liu of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai Office, to extend the deadline indefinitely. The local churches have been doing their best to mediate, and Father Xia Lou also agreed not to object further for the sake of promoting friendship between the two countries. It is hoped that a satisfactory solution can be reached through joint efforts.

Yesterday afternoon, a reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency saw Deputy Director Liu Yunfang at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs office. It was learned that Director Liu had met with Director Li yesterday afternoon. Director Li told Director Liu that the Jinliyuan Wharf case had been largely resolved through diplomatic means, which was gratifying. Regarding the purchase of a portion of the warehouses, only the land price needs to be determined, and there should be no other problems. Since he has just taken office, he is busy with various matters. He will ask Lawyer Gao to inquire about everything tomorrow (i.e., today). The reporter asked Director Liu how the case would proceed after the one-month extension (which expired on September 15) expired. Director Liu replied that he had already informed the French Consul in advance yesterday that the Chinese side could not be held responsible for the delay caused by the priests of Sandetang waiting for a reply from the French General Church, and that he should request a continued extension of the deadline to facilitate public judgment and negotiations. The French Consul had already agreed to this in person and stated this to Lawyer Gao yesterday.

The City is Actively Dividing the Urban Area

The Number of Sections in Densely Populated Areas Will Be Doubled 119

The City Government has specially established a committee to actively carry out the division of urban areas in the city. A few days ago, the committee convened its first meeting to discuss all the issues related to the division of districts in detail. It was noted that the Zhabei and Hunan districts of the city, and the areas adjacent to Zhabei and Hunan, have a large population and a high density of households. In many cases, seven or eight households live in one house, and even one room is divided into several parts to accommodate several families. The crowded conditions are very special. If the regulations of the City Organization Law are followed, with five households as the limit for a neighborhood, and the number of households in the city is calculated as a whole, then the city can be divided into seventy or eighty districts. At a time when the city treasury is in deficit, administrative expenses are already insufficient. In the future, the division into a large number of districts and neighborhoods may hinder municipal facilities, and the city treasury will be unable to cope. It was decided that all of the Southern City and Zhabei, as well as the areas of the Pusong, Fahua, Pengpu, and Wusong districts adjacent to the Southern City and Zhabei, have special circumstances, and it is proposed to double the number of five households per neighborhood in accordance with the special circumstances stipulated in Article 5 of the City Organization Law. It is said that this has been submitted to the City Government for referral to the Ministry of Interior for verification and record.

Water Price Case in the Concession

The Real Estate Association Sends a Letter Requesting the Cancellation of the Approval 120

The Shanghai Real Estate Association sent a letter to the Public Works Department on the 12th, requesting the cancellation of the water price increase case of the Water Company. The original letter is translated below: Respectfully, our association sent a serious protest to the Shanghai Water Company on the 9th of this month, opposing the increase in surcharges, stating that the company's increase in water prices is not allowed, whether in principle or as a temporary expedient. If it is implemented, it will be contrary to the contract signed by your bureau and the company in 1928. Within the time period of the price rate, the provisions of the price shall not be arbitrarily changed. I hope that you will understand the principles of municipal administration in the newspaper, and that all public utilities with natural monopoly properties must be owned by the public. If they are run by private companies, the public must impose proper sanctions. If there is a lack of sanctions, private companies often seek to profit and damage the public interest. The local authorities must provide absolute protection to the interests of individual users and the entire society to prevent the company from being eroded by greed for profit. The only reason the company proposed to increase prices this time is that the exchange rate has plummeted and prices have risen, resulting in a loss of net profit this year and insufficient payment of regular dividends. On this point, our association has the following questions to ask: (1) What is the amount of the so-called insufficient dividend payment? (2) According to the contract, when dividends are insufficient, the savings from the average dividend account must be used to pay. Has the company followed this provision? (3) The current exchange rate has gradually rebounded. Has the company announced that the insufficient dividend payment due to the plummeting exchange rate has been reduced due to the increase in the exchange rate? (4) Is there a provision in the contract that regular dividends must be paid annually at a maximum fixed rate? (5) The price rate period stipulated in the contract is five years. Why did the company request a revision of the price only five years after the contract was signed? Our association does not know whether the company has explained the above questions to your bureau, but it is kept secret from the residents. Now that the company wants to compensate for its losses by increasing prices for the residents, the residents should know the company's current economic situation and the truth about the price increase. It is proposed that your bureau conduct a thorough investigation of all the company's files and accounts in accordance with the special rights granted by Article 23 of the contract, so that the residents can be informed of the company's economic content, so as to await a fair and impartial judgment from the society. At present, please reconsider the price increase proposal, revoke the previous approval, and conduct a revision when the current price rate period expires, taking the interests of all residents as the premise. Any requirements of the company must be approved by the residents. I can't help but look forward to it. Correspondingly, I hope you will check and take care of it.

Yesterday, Tenants in Qingyun Lane Held a Large Petition

Hua Dong Yuan Lüdun is Currently Mediating 121

Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, the tenants' union of Qingyun Lane in Hongkou made a large-scale petition to various institutions. Over 300 evicted tenants participated, and Tang Huilian, Zhou Gan Chen, Gao Jieyuan, and Jiang Xianhe were elected as chief representatives. They prepared a written statement and traveled in five large automobiles. First, they drove to the Fourth District Party Headquarters, where they were received by Committee Member Shen. He agreed to forward their request to higher authorities and strongly advocate for a satisfactory resolution. After a 20-minute discussion, they departed and drove to the Shanghai Special District Court. They were received by Judge Chen, who expressed concern. He stated that the court had read the news reports after the incident and would legally protect the rights of the representatives. The court would not condone any disturbance of the peace. They then drove to the Municipal Party Headquarters, where Comrade Huang Xianggu met with them and stated that the party's principles were to protect the safety and security of the citizens. Regardless of the country of origin, if people use barbaric means to oppress us, the government should be responsible for negotiating and protecting our citizens. The Chinese government values humanity and temporarily allows people to stay to make a living. Unexpectedly, these White Russians dared to be ungrateful and assist in oppressing their hosts, which is unjustifiable. He promised to deal with them severely and instructed the representatives to comfort the petitioning tenants, assuring them to live and work in peace while awaiting a resolution. After a 30-minute discussion, the representatives happily withdrew. They then drove to the Municipal Government, where Committee Member Zhang showed great concern for the people's suffering. He instructed the representatives to comfort the petitioning tenants and not to be misled by rumors, assuring them to wait patiently for a solution. He emphasized that the spirit of public unity must adhere to the regulations on public training to comply with the legal system and not overstep boundaries. As for the landlord's illegal actions that have caused the Chinese people to suffer such humiliation, the government would provide adequate protection and countermeasures to achieve a satisfactory resolution. The discussion was detailed and passionate, lasting about 30 minutes. The representatives expressed their gratitude and took their leave. They then went to the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, but Director Chen was not present. They handed the petition to the transmission office to be forwarded on their behalf. Finally, they drove back to the Public Concession Bureau to see General Manager Edward, but he had already finished work for the day, so they did not meet. The representatives then led all the tenants back to the association headquarters, arriving at 6:00 PM. The text of the petition is recorded below:

To: Mayor Zhang of the Shanghai Municipal Government, Director Chen of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, President Yang of the Shanghai Special District Court, the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters, the Fourth District Party Headquarters, and General Manager Edward of the Shanghai Public Concession Bureau.

We, the members of the association, are submitting this petition regarding the house owner, the British firm New Sassoon, employing White Russian gangsters to forcibly demolish our homes. We request your swift assistance to maintain security and order.

The houses rented by the members of the association from New Sassoon were renovated only 13 years ago and are still in good condition, with no need for reconstruction. However, the firm, greedy for profit, leased the properties to a certain large company and suddenly issued a notice at the end of June, demanding that we move out and hand over the houses by August 31st to facilitate construction. At a time of financial hardship and economic downturn, with dwindling wages and high prices, it is difficult for the members of the association to bear the heavy burden of relocation. Moreover, there are very few vacant houses in Shanghai, making it even harder to find alternative accommodation. Therefore, we have repeatedly written letters and sent representatives. Finally, we entrusted lawyer Chen Tingrui to write a letter, earnestly requesting them to reconsider. However, the firm, blinded by profit, showed no compassion. The members of the association were left with nowhere to turn and appealed for help. Fortunately, organizations such as the Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association wrote to the Public Concession Bureau, requesting impartial handling, preventative measures, and a swift halt to the firm's illegal actions. They also issued an order to all police stations, forbidding them from sending officers to assist in the abuse and avoid causing trouble. We received a reply from the Public Concession Bureau stating that these disputes should be resolved by the court, and the police would only maintain order and enforce court orders. The firm, unable to achieve its goals, suddenly cut off the electricity to our neighborhood on September 1st, attempting to plunge the entire area into darkness. They also requested the water company to stop supplying water, aiming to starve the entire neighborhood into submission. Fortunately, the company, with a strong sense of justice, was not fooled. On September 10th, at 10:00 AM, they hired over 200 Russian gangsters, who swarmed in, destroying property and attacking people. They climbed onto the roofs and demolished houses arbitrarily. They also openly robbed and stole, preventing any resistance. The disorder was immediately reported to the police station, who sent officers to restore order. It is estimated that three people, Miao She-lai, Ye Cheng-lin, and Li A-chang, were injured, and daily necessities, money, and clothing were lost. Such illegal oppression and wanton destruction by the firm, with their inhumanity and disregard for the law, cannot be tolerated by justice and are universally condemned. Furthermore, the Russian gangsters are being used to disrupt the peace. If they are allowed to reside in Shanghai for an extended period, the local area will become increasingly dangerous. In addition to filing a lawsuit with the court to seek due punishment, we are submitting this petition to your government and departments, requesting that you take measures to expel the Russian gangsters, who pose a threat to the security of Shanghai, to protect local security. We also ask for appropriate assistance to protect the legal residential rights of the citizens. We would be eternally grateful.

Dama Evening News says that regarding the negotiation of house demolition in Qingyun Lane, Chongming Road, Hua Dong Yuan Lüdeng of the Public Concession Bureau, considering the seriousness of the situation, has voluntarily stepped forward to mediate. He has contacted the landlord Sassoon several times, and a concrete solution is expected this afternoon (the 15th). The houses in the lane remain in their original state, and the tenants' union posted a notice today advising all tenants to wait patiently for the outcome of the mediation.

Swedish Match Merchants Purchase Japanese Match Factory

Ministry of Industry and Commerce Convenes National Match Industry Conference 122

Swedish matches are sold all over the world, and almost all match industries in various countries have been defeated. Chinese match merchants have also been affected by their competition and are barely surviving. Recently, Swedish merchants purchased the entire Japanese Sui-sei Match Factory. The Japanese Sui-sei Match Factory has its main factory in Japan and two factories in China, one on Gordon Road in Shanghai and one in Zhenjiang, both of which are quite large. The Shanghai Industrial and Commercial Visiting Bureau will convene a meeting of the National Match United Association and major match merchants, including Mr. Liu Hongsheng, at 10:30 AM on the 17th of this month to discuss countermeasures.

Li Zhonggong Officially Takes Office Yesterday

Attends Memorial Week and Reports on Administrative Guidelines 123

Mr. Li Zhonggong, the newly appointed General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, officially arrived at the company and began his duties yesterday. Yesterday morning, Mr. Li attended the company's Memorial Week ceremony and reported on the company's affairs. He stated that after the stabilization of the situation, whatever policy the government adopts towards the company will help its future development. He received a telegram from the Nanjing Telecommunications Reorganization Committee stating that it would be established this Friday, which will provide the company with a responsible reorganization mechanism and increase its strength to promote its future development. Although the list of committee members has not been announced, those appointed by the nation to the reorganization committee will definitely not be high-ranking officials merely in name. The most urgent task for the company is to deal with outstanding payments totaling around 1.6 million taels. He will be responsible for handling the company's affairs from today onwards and will need to raise funds to cover these payments. First, he will settle the outstanding payments from the previous administration of Mr. Zhao, then find ways to repay old and new debts. Once the committee decides on a direction, a fundamental reorganization plan will be developed. In his view, fundamental reorganization is not difficult, but dealing with the current situation is. His standards for personnel and administration are talent, appropriate management, scientific management, elimination of corruption, and integrity. He already stated at the inauguration ceremony that he is committed to integrity. During his three years of service in the Ministry of Communications, he did not take a single penny beyond his salary. Outsiders may view the company as a lucrative position, but he only knows to maintain integrity and will remain unwavering. He also hopes to work with his colleagues towards this goal. Some department heads from the previous administration of Mr. Zhao have firmly resigned. Because the work of the departments is important and cannot be left vacant for a day, others have been appointed to take over. Other employees who have served the company for a long time and have achieved considerable results can continue to serve with peace of mind. Foreign shipping companies employ very few people but are highly efficient because everyone does their best and takes responsibility. In the future, he will base rewards and punishments on the diligence of his colleagues. In short, the company's position is not that of an ordinary shipping company and is of great importance to both the industry and the country. From today onwards, he hopes that his colleagues will work for the party, the country, and the company with peace of mind. No matter what difficulties we encounter, we can overcome them. From today onwards, let us, along with the current situation, wish the company a prosperous future. Mr. Li appointed Yu Zhiming as secretary to handle confidential matters and entrusted him with the seal. Department Head Shen Zhongyi of the Shipping Department will temporarily take over. Staff member Cao Renze was appointed as Assistant of the Shipping Department.

General Manager Li of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Expresses His Views to the Employees of the Five Wharves

The employees' union of the Five Wharves of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, due to the fact that Mr. Li Zhonggong has now taken over, sent representatives to pay their respects yesterday and inquire about the reorganization plan, employee benefits, and unpaid wages. General Manager Li personally received them. The representative of the employees' union, Yu Xianting, spoke first, offering his congratulations and hoping that the comprador system would be completely reformed. General Manager Li then spoke briefly, stating that he had come to reorganize the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company on a mission from the central government and would do so in accordance with the Three Principles of the People and the will of the central government. He can now say a few words that he hopes will be conveyed to all colleagues: (1) He expresses absolute sympathy for the employees' union. (2) He takes full responsibility for the employees' salaries, and unpaid wages will be paid as soon as possible, as this is what employees rely on to make a living. (3) Employee benefits will gradually improve. Finally, Yu said that the employees' union still had some outstanding cases with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, which had been delayed due to the murder of General Manager Zhao and the temporary nature of Mr. Cai's position. Now that Mr. Li is the officially appointed General Manager by the central government, he hopes that all outstanding cases will be resolved as soon as possible. Li replied that he would resolve them in a short period of time after some reorganization and that he also hopes to meet with the responsible persons of the union from time to time to exchange opinions, in order to avoid misunderstandings and to fully understand the situation of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company.

Commander-in-Chief Xiong Sets a Deadline for Eradicating Lake Bandits

Xiong Shihui, the Commander-in-Chief of the Bandit Suppression in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces, in order to eliminate the bandits in Taihu Lake and the Gu-shan Lake, specially appointed Hu Zhengji as the temporary Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression. All the water police and land and water military police in the four counties of Qingpu, Songjiang, Jinshan, and Pinghu will be under his command. If bandits flow into the counties of Wujiang, Fengxian, Shanghai, Jiaxing, Jiashan, and Nanhui, the Bandit Suppression Commander-in-Chief will dispatch the land and water public security teams to deal with them. The deadline for complete eradication is the end of September. Therefore, a major campaign will soon be launched against the bandits' nests to eliminate future troubles.

Compilation of Memorial Week Activities of Various Institutions

The Municipal Executive Committee held the Memorial Week ceremony for Dr. Sun Yat-sen yesterday. After the ceremony, Chairman Pan Gongzhan reported on the major work of various departments and bureaus in the past week, followed by Wu Kaixian's report on party affairs and political affairs during the week. The meeting adjourned after the reports.

The Municipal Government held the Memorial Week ceremony for Dr. Sun Yat-sen yesterday. The Secretary-General presided over the ceremony. Assistant Secretary Chen Kan-cheng reported on the government's situation, followed by Huang Daolin, the head of the Third Section, who reported on the implementation of municipal administration in the past week. Finally, Secretary-General Yu Hongjun supplemented the municipal report. The ceremony ended around 10:00 AM.

The Naval Reorganization Office held the Memorial Week ceremony for Dr. Sun Yat-sen yesterday. All the staff of the office and the special party headquarters attended. Zheng Youyi, the executive committee member of the special party headquarters, presided over the ceremony. Cai Linyong reported on the military, political, and party affairs of the week. The ceremony ended at 11:00 AM.

The Party Headquarters of the Two Roads held its 61st Memorial Week ceremony for Dr. Sun Yat-sen yesterday. Committee Member Zheng Wenli presided over the ceremony. After everyone paid their respects, he reported on party affairs and political affairs. The meeting adjourned after the reports.

The County Reorganization Committee held its 26th Memorial Week ceremony for Dr. Sun Yat-sen yesterday. Tao Yishan presided over the ceremony. The chairman first reported on party affairs and military and political affairs, followed by speeches by various comrades. The meeting adjourned after the ceremony.

The County Government held its Memorial Week ceremony at 9:00 AM yesterday. County Magistrate Yan presided over the ceremony. The chairman reported on the military and political situation in the country and the general work of the government in the past week, followed by reports from various bureaus. The meeting adjourned after the ceremony.

Reply Regarding催兑懋業鈔票 (Promoting the Exchange of Maoye Bank Notes)

First to Exchange One-Yuan Notes 124

"Dear Sirs, We received your letter stating that a significant number of Maoye Bank notes have been issued and urging us to promote their exchange. We forwarded your letter to the Shanghai Bankers' Association, which in turn forwarded it to the Maoye Bank Liquidation Office. According to the reply from the Liquidation Office, they have begun liquidation and will first exchange one-yuan notes. They intend to continue to handle the five-yuan and ten-yuan notes, but the number of five-yuan and ten-yuan notes issued is enormous, and the cash reserves are far short. Therefore, they can only rely on recovering the bank's debts. However, it is very difficult to collect the loans and overdrafts issued by the bank in a short period of time, and the current situation makes it even more difficult. They are currently trying to actively recover the bank's debts and will formulate an exchange plan and publish a notice in Chinese and foreign newspapers as soon as they have collected a certain amount. The Liquidation Office's responsibilities are inherent and need no urging. We have recorded the letter and replied accordingly. We hope that you will check and forward it to the Suzhou General Chamber of Commerce."

Explanation of Chamber of Commerce Organization Issues 125

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce issued the following explanations regarding chamber of commerce organization issues:

Method for Calculating the Increase of Representatives in Trade Associations

The Chamber replied to the Yuanning General Chamber of Commerce: "Dear Sirs, We received your letter of the 13th inquiring why the number of representatives nominated by trade associations in this city has not reached the maximum number stipulated by law, and requesting that we provide a list of the number of representatives nominated by each association, along with three types of formulas for calculating the method of nominating representatives for discussion. After investigation, very few trade associations in this city nominate the maximum number of representatives stipulated by law. This is not due to the undetermined number of employees in the shops belonging to the association, but because the membership fee must also be increased according to Article 48 of our chamber's regulations when the number of representatives is increased. In order to save money, most associations do not nominate the full number of representatives. Article 11 of the Chamber of Commerce Law stipulates that for every 15 additional people, one additional representative may be added. The wording of the law is arbitrary, and the association has the right to waive the right to nominate additional representatives. Our chamber cannot legally force them to nominate the full number of representatives. Therefore, there is no relationship with the calculation method. Regarding the calculation formulas listed in your letter, our chamber believes that this level still needs to be studied. The definition of 'more than fifteen people' in Article 11 of the Chamber of Commerce Law, according to our chamber's interpretation, refers to the total number of employees in the shops belonging to the association exceeding fifteen people during the most recent year's average use. The so-called 'for every 15 additional people' also means that for every 15 people from the sixteenth person onwards, in addition to the basic number of 15 people, one unit should be added, and one additional representative should be nominated. Therefore, according to the example in your letter, if the total number of employees in the shops belonging to a certain association is 210, one representative should be nominated for the basic number of 15 people. The remaining number is 195, which equals 13 units. Therefore, 13 additional representatives should be nominated, for a total of 14. The calculation method is the same regardless of whether there are seven or eight shops in the same industry. This is because, according to Article 8 of the Revised Implementation Rules of the Chamber of Commerce Law, the number of representatives of the association's members should be calculated comprehensively based on the number of employees in the shops belonging to the association. Therefore, the association is the main body, and there is no need to use the number of trade associations as the calculation standard. Whether this humble opinion is appropriate, we hope that you will make a decision early."

Page 14

Employees Do Not Include Apprentices or Workers

The chamber sent a letter to the Yagugi Industry Association: "Dear Sirs, We received your letter of the 13th asking whether the employees filled in the form refer to apprentices and workers in the store calculated together, or whether apprentices and workers are not included. After checking, Article 9 of the revised Implementation Rules of the Chamber of Commerce Law states that the term 'employees' in the preceding article is limited to managers, partners, and shop assistants who directly serve in the business. According to this standard, the workers in the store serve the business indirectly rather than directly, and therefore should not be included. We are sending this letter to inform you."

Two Types of Firms: Members and Representatives

The chamber sent a letter to the Silk and Satin Trade Association: "Dear Sirs, On the 13th of this month, we received Instruction No. 1746 from the Social Affairs Bureau regarding the case of Instruction No. 5607 from the Municipal Government approving the Department of Industry and Commerce's Consultation No. 12415 regarding the reply to the consultation regarding the inquiry from the City Silk and Satin Industry Reorganization Committee about whether restrictions should be imposed on the two types of firms: members and representatives. We have presented this case, which concerns the interpretation of laws and regulations, to the Executive Yuan to consult the Judicial Yuan for interpretation. In addition to waiting for the decree from the Yuan before sending it, we are sending this consultation in advance for your information, etc. We are sending this order for your information, etc."

Guangji Wheel Detained in Wenzhou

Due to the Discovery of a Batch of Military Supplies 130

Since the Min bandits attacked Taishun and Pingyang, the local garrison in Wenzhou has been strictly guarding the waterways. Also, due to the bandit robbery of merchant ships last week, the Wenzhou garrison has formed a inspection fleet to inspect all merchant ships arriving in Wenzhou before they enter the port to prevent the mixing of communists and bandits. The city gates are closed at 9:00 PM at night, prohibiting passage.

Discovery of Military Supplies

The Wenzhou liner "Guangji" of the China Merchants Bureau loaded passengers and cargo in Shanghai on Friday of last week and sailed to Wenzhou. When the ship arrived at the Wenzhou wharf on Sunday, the inspection team of the local garrison boarded the ship and conducted a thorough search. In the hidden compartment under the platform on the second floor, they found a batch of illegally transported military supplies (the amount is unknown). The soldiers immediately transported the supplies back to the headquarters and began investigating the person responsible for the illegal transport.

Crew Member Flees

At the time of the discovery of the military supplies, the shipowner and others were unaware of the source of the supplies. They promised to investigate the person responsible for the illegal transport and remove the supplies from the "Guangji." Lin Funeng, the tally clerk of the "Guangji," suddenly fled, showing his guilt and attempting to evade responsibility.

Ship Detained

Local garrison officials were furious upon learning of Lin Funeng's disappearance. They considered the matter to be related to the illegal transport of military supplies and could not simply allow the ship to leave because one crew member had fled. They ordered the "Guangji" to be detained and demanded that the shipowner hand over Lin. Shipowner Tang negotiated with the army and requested permission to unload the cargo, as the goods of merchants would be delayed, in addition to assisting in the pursuit of Lin. However, the army had not yet agreed. Yesterday, shipowner Tang sent an urgent telegram to the Shanghai Bureau to report the situation and request negotiations. The bureau has reportedly telegraphed Wenzhou, first requesting that the cargo be unloaded and that the ship not be detained, and then promising to assist in the pursuit of the fugitive crew member. Detailed Report on Yongning Wheel Being Robbed

Four Escort Soldiers Killed 131

This newspaper has already reported that merchant ships have been robbed by bandits in Wenzhou waters. After investigation by reporters from various sources, the details of the case are as follows:

Bandits Mixed Into Ship

The ship robbed was the "Yongning" wheel. This ship is a dedicated line between Ningbo and Wenzhou and is owned by the Yongning Company. Last week (ie, the 7th of this month), when the ship left Wenzhou to return to Ningbo, four bandits dressed as passengers had already mixed into the ship. The rest of the bandits were waiting along the way. When the ship arrived at Shitang, Wenzhou waters, the bandits on the ship waved their scarves to signal the large gang of pirates. More than a hundred pirates chased and boarded the ship from a sailboat, and the great robbery began.

Circumstances of Shitang Robbery

When the large gang of pirates swarmed onto the ship, they first occupied the captain's and driver's room. There were eight escort soldiers on the ship, four in uniform and four in plain clothes due to being off duty. Upon hearing the alarm, they each grabbed a gun to resist the bandits. Unexpectedly, they could not defeat the numerous bandits. The four soldiers in uniform were shot dead by the bandits at the time. The remaining four soldiers abandoned their weapons and fled into the boiler room, all of whom survived. At this point, the bandits began to rob the passengers and crew of their luggage, money, and belongings, all of which were looted.

Kidnapping More Than Thirty People

The purpose of the bandits' robbery of the ship was only one wealthy merchant from Wenzhou. When the robbery occurred, the wealthy merchant quickly took off his silk clothes and fled into the engine room, smearing his face with coal to pretend to be a stoker. The bandits searched everywhere but could not find him. They suspected that he had not boarded the ship and kidnapped more than thirty people from the passengers and crew with slightly more luggage, along with the stolen goods, and drove them onto the bandit boat.

Returning to Wenzhou After Robbery

The Yili wheel of this port, which returned to Shanghai from Wenzhou, passed through Shitang and saw that Yongning was still there. Yili suspected that Yongning had arrived in Ningbo and was returning to Wenzhou. At first, they did not expect to encounter bandits on the way and did not go to Ningbo. The shipowner of the Yongning wheel only re-hoisted the anchor after the bandits left. Instead of going to Ningbo, they turned back to Wenzhou and reported the incident to the customs officials in front of the Ouhai Customs. It is now heard that the Zhejiang Offshore Patrol Hall has sent a warship to pursue the missing kidnapped people. There has been no news of them so far. It is said that the loss of money and goods amounts to tens of thousands of yuan.

The Clearing and Transporting Business Association Actively Opposes 132

The Social Affairs Bureau Mediates Another Sino-Japanese Labor Dispute Yesterday

Final Decision Today 133

The Shanghai Pudong Japan-China Cotton Mill labor dispute was previously [illegible] held by the City Party Department and the Public Security Bureau. All details were recorded in this newspaper at the time. Due to excessive disputes between labor and management, a resolution could not be reached immediately. Regarding worker treatment, the workers claimed that the mill's treatment was the lowest, while the Japanese side stated that the mill treated workers better than other factories. All mediation committee members believed it necessary to investigate, so they announced a second mediation session to be held on Monday (yesterday) morning. Representatives from the City Party Department were to investigate the treatment of workers in various Japanese-owned cotton mills in Shanghai. Yesterday marked the date of the second mediation session. The representatives from both sides in attendance were the Director of the Mediation Section of the City Social Affairs Bureau, Guo Yongxi, Zhang Yaoming from the City Party Department (later replaced by Mao Yun), Wang Guoxian from the City Public Security Bureau, recorder Wang Zhichin, and representatives from the management side, including the head of the Japan-China Mill, Yu Jingzheng, Sichun from the Japanese Cotton Mill Association, and Oikawa, the Personnel Section Chief of the Japan-China Mill. The labor representatives were Zhao Bi, Yu Qixiang, and others. After the formalities, the City Party Department representative reported on the investigation, stating that the treatment in Japanese-owned cotton mills under the same Japan-China capital was the same as in the Japan-China Mill. However, other factories, such as the Inland and External mills, were better than the Japan-China Mill and offered so-called contracted work bonuses and special bonuses in addition to the original wages. Director Guo then explained to the management side, stating that the Japan-China Mill workers held a general meeting yesterday and, after repeated persuasion, had already made concessions. The demand for wages during the strike period had been reduced from two months to two weeks. Regarding the increase in rice subsidies, they only requested that the factory provide each person with eight to ten yuan per month during the strike period until October, and that the original two fen night meal allowance not be canceled. He added that these concessions had reached their limit and urged them to give the matter careful consideration and resolve this point before continuing to discuss other issues. The management side still refused, firmly insisting on canceling the two fen night meal allowance and strongly opposing the wages for the two-week strike period, stating that they had to obey the chairman and could not rashly agree. Even when Director Guo showed them the record book quoting his own words, it had no effect. At the same time, the labor representatives also stated that they would not budge even a little from the agreed-upon scope. At that time, the situation was on the verge of collapse. Later, the Japanese side voluntarily took all the terms back for discussion and promised to return to the bureau at 10:00 am tomorrow (today) after the chairman's approval. Director Guo then drafted six points: (1) The Japan-China Cotton Mill workers' request to the Japanese side to increase rice subsidies will be temporarily suspended. Starting from September, the factory will issue each person a monthly bonus of eight yuan until October. (2) Each worker who completes half a month of day work must be rewarded with one and a half days' wages. Those who complete one week of day work and one week of night work will receive two days' wages plus two fen night allowance for each night. (3) Wages may not be issued directly when the stored work is insufficient. (4) The case of the factory dismissing workers Yu Qixiang and six others will be submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau by this committee to send personnel to investigate and verify. (5) The management will issue four days' wages to each person for the strike period. (6) If both parties can agree to sign the above points, work will be resumed at 9:00 am on Thursday (the 18th). All points were handed over to the labor and management sides for circulation. The management side immediately agreed to take them back for consultation. This mediation meeting can be said to have come to an end. If both parties cannot sign today, it will be a sign of a breakdown, and the Social Affairs Bureau will no longer hold mediation sessions and will submit a request to the City Government for arbitration. The Anglo-American factory went on strike.

Yesterday's Mediation a Success 134

The old factory of the Shanghai Anglo-American Tobacco Company, the tin packaging workers, went on strike because the management dismissed worker Bao Yangzhou without reason. Last Saturday, the Party and government sides were prepared to go for mediation, but the head of the factory was out of town due to being late. Yesterday, Qiu Peihao from the Social Affairs Bureau, Wu Jiaze from the City Party Department, and others rejoined with Chen Peide and Gu Ruofeng, the standing committee members of the labor union, to negotiate with the factory head, Gelandete, demanding that worker Bao Yangzhou be restored to his original job and that wages be paid as usual during the strike period. At that time, the head allowed Bao Yangzhou's work to be restored, but he had to be transferred to another room. If he was dissatisfied, he would be allowed to return to a suitable position after a week. Wages for one day of the strike period were acknowledged, calculated from 9:00 am to 2:00 pm. The representatives from both sides negotiated until their tongues were dry, but the head insisted on the original proposal. The representative from the Social Affairs Bureau and the representative declared that the matter would be discussed after the union convened a meeting of workers, and then negotiations would continue. The head agreed to wait at the factory for a reply and postponed his trip across the river by one hour. The union then convened a meeting of tin packaging factory workers at 4:00 pm, chaired by Chen Peide, who reported on everything and invited Qiu Peihao from the Social Affairs Bureau to attend and provide guidance. At that time, the workers felt that Bao Yangzhou's work had not been completely restored in accordance with the union's requirements, but they were satisfied. However, they insisted that the item of wages for only one day during the strike period must be fully paid. The representative from the Social Affairs Bureau immediately respected the union's wishes and returned to the factory to negotiate. It was not until about 6:00 pm that the head fully agreed, and the workers also decided to resume work today.

Local News

Death of Russian Child Lost at Sea 137

From the Mouth of a Companion Child

The Police Believe Drowning is Undoubted

His Mother Anxiously Awaits Her Son's Return

The Actions of the Small Boat Owner Are Highly Suspicious

Three days ago, this newspaper carried a news item about the fearless spirit of three Russian children, stating that eight-and-a-half-year-old Lukonsky served as first mate, and twelve-year-old Gravsky was the shipowner. The three children set off in a mighty manner. The ancients had the ambition to ride the long wind and break through thousands of miles of waves, and these young children were able to practice their lives of breaking through the wind and waves. Calling it a fearless spirit is truly accurate and unwavering. Therefore, this news item attracted the attention of readers after it was published. The incident occurred on the first of this month, and the next day, two children were sent home by the water patrol team. However, first mate Lukonsky was nowhere to be found, becoming a suspicious case. His mother, Mrs. Gardon, was very anxious. In addition to asking the police and various newspapers to search, she also sent telegrams to relatives and friends in other ports to pay attention. Yesterday, the reporter suddenly received a message stating that Lukonsky's disappearance involved the two Russian children who were traveling with him, and that Kang had already drowned. The reporter believed that there must be twists and turns inside the matter and that it was interesting, so he visited Lukonsky's mother, Mrs. Jia, at her residence on Mercer Road, and learned about the outline of the matter.

Drowned in Huangpu. The so-called first mate Lukonsky lives with his mother at No. 319 Mercer Road, French Concession. When the reporter first visited at around 8:00 pm, only lights were leaking from the windows on the floor, and it was quiet as if no one lived there. When he knocked on the door, he suddenly saw a small note on the lintel with the English words "Beware of dogs." The reporter became wary. However, after tapping for a long time, there was no sound, let alone the sound of dogs. The reporter was very frustrated and changed to the back door. Then, the Chinese characters "Beware of ferocious dogs" were written in white powder on the back door. The reporter was even more frightened. He thought that since the family kept many dogs and marked them as ferocious, then the little master's adventurous nature was probably not accidental. He wanted to knock on the door, but there was no response, so he had to return in disappointment. The second time he arrived at around 10:00 pm, the light from the building shone, and he could see the beautiful furnishings in the room. After entering the room, he met the hostess, Mrs. Jia, who looked sad and worried. However, two puppies jumped in front of and behind the hostess, looking very gentle and friendly. The reporter recalled the "Beware of dogs" sign in front of the door and the "Beware of ferocious dogs" sign behind the door, and could not help but smile silently. After sitting down, Mrs. Jia said that the news of her son's drowning was indeed true, but the exact circumstances of the matter were not clear. There were a total of three people traveling together. Her son was eight and a half years old, one was nine years old, and the oldest was nine years old. However, the one with the highest height was the nine-year-old, followed by her son, and the ten-year-old was very short. The news of Kang's drowning was received at 3:00 pm yesterday, and the location was Huangpu.

Clothes Cannot Be Found. Later, she mentioned that the oldest child often came to her to take Lukonsky out to play, and they had a close relationship. However, sometimes there were inevitably mischievous actions. When Mrs. Jia spoke to this point, her words were choked and her heart seemed extremely sad. When she spoke about her son's situation when he encountered the disaster, she felt even more sad. She said, "I once asked the child who returned about what happened to the clothes, shoes, and pants of my son, who had died, which could be used as evidence. The child replied that Kang was still wearing his shoes when he entered the water, and as for the clothes, they were used as floats and had already been taken off." Mrs. Jia's appearance seemed to still not believe that her son had suffered such a quick demise. Since it was late, the reporter briefly said a few words and then took his leave. The two small, white dogs still accompanied their pitiful hostess to the door to see him off.

The Truth is Also Bizarre. According to the police interrogation, Lukonsky's drowning seems to be beyond doubt. As for the cause of death, according to the report of the two children who returned, the situation was this: The ship was sailing in the Huangpu River near Donggou. The three children left the ship to swim, and the first mate, Lukonsky, somehow drowned. However, whether there is any suspicion in it is still under investigation. One of the children in the same group reportedly had very bad behavior in peacetime. He often had strange ideas during games. Once, he hid Lukongsky in one place and then went to his mother to tell him that he was missing. Lukongsky's mother gave this child a few small silver dollars before he was sent back, which seemed to have a preliminary kidnapping meaning. Now, this bad news is really unfortunate. The implication of this child is out of our conjecture.

Pirates Leave Da'an Port Outside Wusongkou 139

Da'an Port, at the junction of Nantong and Haimen counties outside Wusongkou, was occupied by a large number of pirates, and the situation was extremely rampant. The Jiangsu Water Police Provincial Public Security Team Wusong Fourth District Chief Zhang Han repeatedly sent the 17th and 18th patrol boats and gunboats under his jurisdiction to the port to suppress them. The details were recorded in this newspaper. However, because the port forks were arranged within more than ten miles around Da'an Port, the shifting sands flooded constantly. Therefore, although the water police repeatedly went to suppress them, the pirates stubbornly resisted and the water police were outnumbered. Up to now, they have not been able to suppress them. Unexpectedly, the pirates dispatched pirate ships in all directions to rob civilian ships in various oceans, totaling more than 50 ships, plus the original pirate ships, there were a total of 100 ships, all of which were docked at the north port of Da'an Port. At about 10:00 pm that night, all the bandits, more than 700 people, gathered in an orderly manner and transported all the military equipment, baggage, food, and valuable stolen goods to the port and loaded them on the pirate ships. The bandits were deployed until 5:00 am yesterday before they were ready, and then they boarded the ships in groups, raised their sails, and went to the East China Sea. One day before the pirates left, they sent a letter to the local authorities, saying that the army had been ordered to depart and that all the civilian houses occupied in Da'an Port should be sent to be taken over. Now there is no trace of bandits in the port, and the whereabouts of more than 20 men, women, and children who were kidnapped by those people are unknown. Most of them have been taken away by the pirates. The purpose of the pirates' sudden departure from Da'an Port is difficult to guess, and where they are going is temporarily unknown. After Jiangsu Water Police Provincial Public Security Team Wusong Fourth District Chief Zhang Han was reported yesterday, he was concerned that Da'an Port had numerous port forks and a dangerous terrain, fearing that the bandits would come back after they left, or that another group of pirates would go to occupy it. The consequences would be unimaginable. Therefore, he has urgently ordered the 17th Team Captain Gong Jinqin and the 18th Team Captain Lin Cha to quickly send multiple patrol boats to the port to patrol and defend each port.

The Shanghai Land Bureau Seriously Inspects Field Certificates 140

The Shanghai Land Bureau is earnestly carrying out the work of reorganizing land, and the inspection of field certificates is also extremely serious. The field certificates issued by Shanghai County in the fifth year of Xianfeng have not been replaced for a long time, and there are many counterfeit certificates. The Shanghai Land Bureau affixed the fake certificate invalidation stamp on all the field certificates sent for verification by the Jiangsu Shanghai Local Court and the Special Zone Local Court, as well as those who changed the Yongzu contract and Chinese who applied for land certificates, as long as there were fake certificates. However, after the fake certificate was found and stamped as invalid, if the property rights part has other strong evidence, it will still be recognized, so although the crackdown is strict, the people are not resentful. Recently, Wang Guantong requested to sell the fake certificate of Wang Zhizhong's household, No. 57, Eleven Qiu, Yinzitu Di Ziwei, Jiangwan District, to the real estate contract distribution office in the district. The office was detained and handed over to the land bureau for investigation together with the fake certificate. It is heard that the land bureau has prepared a document to transfer it to the Jiangsu Shanghai Local Court to thoroughly investigate the origin of Wang Guantong's fake certificate and arrest the person who forged the field certificate and handle it according to law. The bureau's serious inspection will eliminate fake certificates in the future, and the credibility of land certificates will inevitably increase day by day.

Price Change of Shanghai South Public Bus Route 4 141

The Original Price of Each Ticket Increased by Two Cents

Changed to Incremental One Cent Per Stop

Shanghai South Public Bus Route 4 runs between Xujiahui and the Hongqiao Road Airport. The fare for the route was originally 5 cents at the start to 40 cents. In July of this year, the company reported to the Municipal Public Utility Bureau for approval to increase the fares of all routes by 2 cents per ticket due to the strange price of gold and the soaring price of gasoline. Therefore, Route 4 should be 7 cents from the starting station to 42 cents. However, the company ultimately believed that the route had suffered huge losses over the years and that an increase of two cents per ticket was not enough to make up for it, and that the route was a long-distance route and was different from other routes. It repeatedly stated the difficult situation to the bureau and asked to be allowed to increase one cent per stop. It is heard that the bureau verified that it was true and had already submitted it to the Municipal Government for approval.

The Truth of the Case Against Dr. Gu 144

The Municipal Government Orders the Return of His License First

The Court Investigates and Orders His Release Pending Further Action

Fang Yongtai, a Jiangbei resident, brought his son, who had developed a sore boil on his forehead a month prior, to Dr. Gu Xiaoyan, a Chinese medicine practitioner specializing in surgery on Zixia Road. Dr. Gu diagnosed the child with a high fever and proceeded to treat the boil with surgery while advising the parents to urgently seek treatment for the internal symptoms at a pediatrics clinic, warning of possible convulsions if delayed. However, due to financial constraints, the Fang family did not seek the care of a pediatric doctor. The next day, the child indeed suffered a convulsion and was brought back to Dr. Gu. Dr. Gu observed that the child's condition was critical and, upon learning that internal treatment had not been sought, urged them again to seek pediatric care. Subsequently, the child died from the convulsion, and the family reported the incident to the Bureau of Health. The Bureau, fearing medical malpractice, temporarily suspended Dr. Gu's license and forwarded the entire case file to the Municipal Government for review. After a thorough review, the Municipal Government concluded that the child's death was not necessarily due to Dr. Gu's negligence and ordered the Bureau of Health to reinstate Dr. Gu's license. However, recognizing that the case involved a human life, the Municipal Government deemed it necessary to thoroughly investigate the facts and transferred the case to the Shanghai District Court for investigation. After investigation, the Prosecutor's Office ordered Dr. Gu's release pending further action. It is reported that the Fang family, grieving the loss of their child, acted out of temporary distress and made things difficult for Dr. Gu. Dr. Gu, on the other hand, had diligently provided treatment and was not negligent. The Chinese Medicine Association also conducted a thorough investigation and confirmed that Dr. Gu had done everything properly. Dr. Gu has since received his license back and has resumed seeing patients as usual.

Saving His Sister from Drowning: Ni Miaosheng Tragically Perishes 146

Ni Miaosheng, a 26-year-old boatman from Wusong Yunzaobang, had a 13-year-old sister named Miaoling. Yesterday, around 5:00 AM, the brother and sister were loading cargo onto their boat to take it to port. While rowing along the Yunzaobang near the western end of Tang Bridge, the oar rope suddenly broke. Miaoling accidentally fell into the river. The current was strong, and she was swept westward. Her brother, Ni Miaosheng, saw this from the front of the boat and was greatly alarmed. He quickly grabbed a bamboo pole and jumped into the river to save her. As a result, Miaoling grabbed the end of the pole and pulled herself into the boat, avoiding drowning. Ni Miaosheng, who was somewhat skilled in swimming, struggled in the water while trying to save his sister. After Miaoling climbed onto the boat, her brother disappeared. Then, his bamboo pole was seen floating on the water's surface, indicating that he had drowned. Miaoling shouted for help. Nearby boats heard her cries and came to rescue Ni Miaosheng. However, he had swallowed too much water and could not be revived. He was dead, though his body was still warm. His elderly mother arrived upon hearing the news and mourned over his body. The family prepared a coffin on the boat and proceeded with the burial arrangements.

Sisters Nearly Abducted 149

Zhu Lushi's Sinister Intentions

Lu Genhe Escorts Them Back to Shanghai

Zhang Jinbao, a local resident, has two daughters, Gen Di, 16, and Lan Ying, 14, who both work at the Yong'an Cotton Mill on Maigen Road in western Shanghai. On the morning of the eighth of this month, at 6:00 AM, the sisters were on their way to the factory from their home at No. 901 Xiaoshadu Road when they were lured by their neighbor, Zhu Lushi. They went with her to the North Railway Station. After a while, Zhu Lushi's paramour, Zhu Jintang, arrived and bought three train tickets. Zhu Lushi took the two girls onto the train and they arrived in Kunshan, where they stayed at an inn. The next day, they walked to Luxiang Village in Changshu and stayed at the home of Lu Genhe, Zhu Lushi's nephew. Zhu Lushi told her nephew that the two girls accompanying her had been purchased for 400 yuan and would be married as daughters-in-law in the future. She asked him to temporarily accommodate them at his home. When the two girls heard this, they realized they had been abducted and cried loudly. Lu Genhe asked the girls what had happened and learned the truth. He disapproved of his aunt's actions. Zhu Lushi, seeing that Genhe was not on her side, fled secretly that evening. The next day, Genhe, unsure of his aunt's whereabouts, sent the two girls back to Shanghai by steamer. In fact, Zhu Lushi knew that her nephew would not tolerate her actions and that her plan would be exposed. She had already planned to retaliate. That night, she secretly returned to Kunshan and took a train to Shanghai. She went directly to the Zhang family and asked why their daughters were suddenly in Luxiang Village, Changshu. She claimed to have just seen them there. Zhang, who had been searching for his daughters since their disappearance, was about to go look for them. Zhu Lushi claimed that since they had been abducted, it was possible that the abductors had taken them elsewhere and that they should wait at the various docks. Zhang then ordered his wife, Guo, to wait at the Suzhou River dock with Zhu Lushi, while Zhang and Zhu Lushi's paramour, Zhu Jintang, rushed to Luxiang Village. When they arrived at Lu's house, they learned that the girls had already been taken back to Shanghai by Lu. They immediately returned together, while Lu arrived at the port by steamer with the two girls. They were seen by the girls' mother as soon as they disembarked and were taken home together. Zhang and Zhu returned by train. When the train arrived at the North Station and they were walking along the border road, Zhu suddenly pointed to Zhang to a sentry at No. 1475 and accused him of robbing him. Zhang was arrested by the sentry and taken to the Huisi Police Station. After learning the truth, the police chief determined that the case fell under the jurisdiction of the Gordon Road Police Station and transferred Zhu to that station. After investigation, the police arrested Zhu Lushi. Yesterday morning, Zhang Jinbao and his wife, as well as the two girls and the witness Lu Genhe, were brought to the Special District Court. After a thorough investigation by Judge Wu Tingqi, Zhu Lushi and Zhu Jintang were found guilty of two counts of conspiring to abduct women under the age of 20 from those with parental rights for profit. Each charge carried a sentence of two years in prison, with a total sentence of three years for each. Zhang Gendi and Zhang Lanying were allowed to be taken back by their father, Zhang Jinbao.

An Economical Way to Enjoy the Moon and Watch the Tide 157

The tea house opened the door and released him, and he went to the Fuzhou Road patrol station to report the incident and request assistance in apprehending the thief.

Special Article

Industrial Rationalization (Continuation 4) Cheng Zhenjun 168

As for worker unemployment, it is even less the fault of rationalization. Currently, the countries with the most unemployment are Germany, with about three million people, followed by the United Kingdom, with about two million people. France can be said to have no unemployment. Before the European War, Germany had only 18 million workers, but now it has 22.5 million. This means that industrial rationalization has increased the number of workers by 4.5 million. The reason for the large number of unemployed is that Germans in the ceded territories, not forgetting their homeland, have rushed back to their hometowns, numbering about one million. In addition, the army used to have 750,000 people, but now only 100,000 are retained. Furthermore, there were hundreds of thousands of people manufacturing military equipment, but now they have all changed professions. This is the reason for the sudden increase in unemployment in Germany. The United Kingdom has been very slow in adopting rationalization. The coal and iron industries are the basic industries of the United Kingdom, and they are in contact and competition with the most developed rationalization in Germany and the United States everywhere. However, because the prices are so different, British goods are extremely difficult to sell. In addition, the best markets in the world, such as China and India, are in a state of unrest, making it even more difficult for British industry to develop. Therefore, the unemployment of British workers cannot be blamed on rationalization. The Englishman Uickrw, in his book "The Meaning of Rationalization," painfully stated that the failure of the United Kingdom to vigorously implement rationalization has led to difficulties in industry and commerce, which further proves that rationalization is not the cause of worker unemployment. Moreover, France has specifically set up agencies to implement rationalization, and workers have not lost their jobs. It can be seen that rationalization can make industry prosper. Once industry can prosper, workers will not lose their jobs. Therefore, it can be said that rationalization can prevent workers from losing their jobs, but it is absolutely unreasonable to say that rationalization causes workers to lose their jobs. I have already described the origin, meaning, plan, and functions of rationalization in detail. Now, I will briefly contribute some humble opinions on how our country should start to proceed, to end my article. Our country's industry is young and lacks organization and talent everywhere, and the government and the people have never had a habit of cooperation. Therefore, we can only start with research. The central government should set up an Industrial Rationalization Research Association, and each province and city should set up a Research Association. The government should invite people from the industrial sector with knowledge and reputation to conduct joint research. However, two important points should be noted: (1) Broadly raise funds; (2) Hire several specialists to be solely responsible for various research tasks without holding other positions. Then, collect books, magazines, and newspapers from various countries regarding rationalization, study them in detail, and communicate with the League of Nations and rationalization agencies in various countries, as well as organizations and groups related to rationalization. Then, understand the actual situation in China, consider what should be publicized first, what should be investigated first, what should be organized first, where should experimental laboratories be set up, what matters should be sent abroad for contact, how to disseminate the results of research to various industries, how to make various industries adopt rationalization, how to cultivate the talents needed by the industrial sector, and other issues. The government representatives and industrial leaders should pass the proposals put forward by the specialized researchers through meetings, and then they can be put into practice. This is the driving force for rationalization. As for implementation, it is still a matter for the industrial sector itself. The government and this agency are only in a position to assist and guide. Alas, our country's national character is extremely decadent. Most government officials consider it a skill to get by with perfunctory measures. Industrial leaders are content with the status quo and are too modest to take action. Young people only engage in clamoring and are unwilling to conduct specialized research. Compared with the American's courage and pursuit of efficiency, the German's meticulous scientific research and adherence to order, and the Englishman's deep, decisive, self-respect, and self-esteem, the difference is truly immeasurable. We should urgently abandon the bad habits of sluggishness and procrastination and strive to uplift ourselves. We should also earnestly guard against empty, lofty, and far-reaching fantasies and focus on research. This industrial rationalization is the touchstone for our nation's revitalization, the savior of industrial decline, a major reform in economic organization, and a good opportunity for cooperation between the government and the people. I hope that the government, the industrial sector, and the general public in our country will rise up and work together to achieve the suggestions made by the International Economic Conference. China is fortunate, and the world is fortunate.
